Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support

BACKGROUND
The Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA), which is a component of the Department of Homeland Security (DHS), manages the National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP) and a range of programs designed to reduce future losses to homes, businesses, schools, public buildings and critical facilities from floods, earthquakes, tornadoes and other natural disasters. FEMA focuses on breaking the cycle of disaster damage, reconstruction, and repeated damage. Mitigation efforts initiated by FEMA provide value to the American people by creating safer communities and reducing loss of life and damage to property. A partial list of mitigation activities includes those listed in Table 1.

Mitigation Activities of the NFIP
       Acquiring damaged homes or businesses in flood-prone areas, relocating the structures, and returning the property to open space, wetlands or recreational uses Adopting zoning ordinances that steer development away from areas subject to flooding, storm surge or coastal erosion Building community shelters and tornado safe rooms to help protect people in their homes, public buildings and schools in hurricane- and tornado-prone areas Complying with or exceeding NFIP Floodplain Management Regulations Educating communities on how they can reduce their vulnerability to natural hazard events Enforcing building codes, flood-proofing requirements, seismic design standards and wind-bracing requirements for new construction or repairing existing buildings Retrofitting public buildings to withstand hurricane-strength winds or earthquakes

Table 1 Mitigation Activities of the NFIP

FEMA's Federal Insurance and Mitigation Administration (FIMA) is committed to improving the NFIP by enhancing its efficiency and effectiveness of operation through well-defined strategic business priorities, enabled by well thought out business processes. To accomplish this, constant review and improvement of processes that support the NFIP are needed. Similarly, FEMA desires to utilize the most appropriate Information Technology (IT) capabilities which should be flexible and responsive in ways that help the NFIP reduce costs in processing policies across the program.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 6

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support

DEFINITIONS
SYNOPSIS: It is expected that the reader will review the definitions shown below in order to fully understand this document. The document has been constructed to convey the breadth and complexity of the NFIP with regard to the recordkeeping, reporting and communications activities that must be undertaken to support this important national program. The specific volumes of each activity have not been provided; rather, volumes that are intended to enhance understanding of levels of effort, complexity or experience have been shown. The information presented herein describes the activities that FEMA requires to be performed to administer the NFIP in a manner consistent with all relevant acts of Congress, standards, guidelines, directives and manuals. It should be noted that the standards, guidelines and directives incorporate by reference subsidiary information that also must be adhered to. DEFINITIONS: The following definitions apply to the items, responsibilities, policies and procedures outlined in this document. This document makes liberal use of these definitions throughout.

Definitions
1316 Section 1316 of the National Flood Insurance Act of 1968, as amended, provides for the denial of flood insurance coverage for any property which the Administrator finds has been declared by a duly constituted State or local authority to be in violation of State or local floodplain management regulations. Actuarial Information System -- A subsystem of the SOR that manages the actuarial data and provides analytical and reporting on said data. Bureau and Statistical Agent -- General term that applies to the support provided to the WYO companies, their support vendors, the DSA contractor, or other stakeholders as they provide NFIP-required information and reporting. BureauNet -- Public facing website maintained by Contractor for the NFIP WYOs and DSA to view NFIP data. Sometimes referred to as the BSA site. Coastal Barrier Resource Act -- Protects coastal areas that serve as barriers against wind and tidal forces caused by coastal storms, and serves as habitat for aquatic species. Change Control Board -- A committee that makes decisions regarding whether or not proposed changes to a hardware or software project should be implemented. In short any changes to the Baseline Requirements agreed with the client, should be taken up by project team on approval from this committee. Configuration Management -- A systems engineering process for establishing and maintaining consistency of a product's performance, functional and physical attributes with its requirements, design and operational information throughout its life. Community Master File -- The community files contain information in such categories as CRS, suspensions, withdrawals/annexes, probation, map panels/suffixes, flood zones and county data. Users without secured access can only review information.

In this document, refers to the organizational considerations that must be taken into account if the facility that the Contractor identifies as its primary facility is unavailable. Flood insurance premium rates are discounted to reflect the reduced flood risk resulting from the community actions. Calendar day of twenty four (24) hours, as opposed to business day of eight (8) hours, unless otherwise specified. Direct Servicing Agent -- Vendor who is employed by FEMA to provide agent and policy holder support for agents and policies otherwise unaffiliated with a WYO.

Definitions
Federal Information Security Management Act -- A United States federal law enacted in 2002 as Title III of the E-Government Act of 2002 (Pub.L. 107­347, 116 Stat. 2899). The act recognized the importance of information security to the economic and national security interests of the United States. [1] The act requires each federal agency to develop, document, and implement an agency-wide program to provide information security for the information and information systems that support the operations and assets of the agency, including those provided or managed by another agency, contractor, or other source. Freedom of Information Act -- FOIA is a federal statute that provides the public with the right to request access to records in the possession of federal agencies in the Executive Branch. FOIA establishes a presumption that records are accessible to the people. (Some exemptions apply.) In general, the FOIA requires an agency to respond to FOIA requests within 20 business days after the office that maintains the responsive records receives the request. Flood Regional Office -- Provides a local presence in the affected area and supports the WYO companies, the NFIP Servicing Agent, and various federal, state, and local officials in providing answers to claims coverage questions, forms for claims handling, and survey and statistical input. Facility Security Officer -- Facility security officers are in charge of handling safety at locations such as government buildings and/or public facilities. An FSO's responsibility is to ensure that the premises are safe and that everyone on the property has a legal right to be there. File Transfer Protocol -- A website that is used to transfer information to or from Contractor. Generally Accepted Accounting Principles -- The common set of accounting principles, standards and procedures that are used to compile financial statement information and represent the commonly accepted ways of recording and reporting accounting and financial information. Government Accountability Office -- The U.S. Government Accountability Office (GAO) is an independent, nonpartisan agency that works for Congress. It supports the Congress in meeting its constitutional responsibilities and to help improve the performance and ensure the accountability of the federal government for the benefit of the American people. Geographic Information System -- Computer system designed to capture, store, manipulate, analyze, manage, and present all types of geographical data. The U.S. federal government. Loss Allocation Expense -- Loss expenses other than fees paid to adjusters. This includes LAE special engineering expenses, legal fees, or the cost of an appraisal. Letter Of Credit -- Funds utilized to reimburse the Contractor for approved travel LOC expenses related to conducting claims re-inspections, costs associated with FRO leasing space, and other COR pre-approved expenses associated with flooding disasters. Table 2 Definitions

SCOPE
FEMA is responsible for administering the WYO program, which includes NFIP operating policies, establishing rates, designating eligible communities, developing reporting requirements, and creating auditing specifications. There are approximately 5.6 million NFIP policies in force, with over $1.25 trillion of coverage in force. These policies are sold and serviced through over 80 private PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 13

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support insurance companies participating in the WYO program, all of whom must report every transaction to the NFIP. The WYO companies are the primary vehicle for selling, delivering and servicing flood insurance policies, and they are responsible for approximately 75% of NFIP policies in force. The WYO companies have been invaluable in the NFIP's effort to increase the flood insurance policy base, increase the geographic distribution of policyholders, improve service to policyholders as well as insurance agents, and enhance the NFIP's ability to settle claims promptly and fairly in post-catastrophe environments. FEMA requires a contractor, hereinafter referred to as "Contractor," to provide program management, insurance services, financial services, and System of Record (SOR) operations, maintenance, and support services of the legacy IT system environment, all in support of the NFIP. This means that FEMA requires a wide array of business and IT services. The Contractor serves as a point of contact and provides support for the Write Your Own (WYO) program and NFIP Direct Servicing Agent (DSA). A Monthly Technical Progress Narrative (MTPN) created by the Contractor provides a comprehensive report of the previous month's activities and provides valuable information to FIMA management. In addition to the services listed above, the Contractor is a source of information for the WYO insurance companies and the DSA contractor as they work to provide the information required by the NFIP. The Contractor will also engage in support activities that include tracking, collecting, disseminating, maintaining, and updating information on the NFIP and the WYO companies. The Contractor must reconcile the policy details and produce accurate reports to ensure the financial integrity of the program; this involves about $3.2 billion in annual premium collections that must be accurately accounted for. FEMA undertakes these responsibilities in cooperation with participating NFIP communities and the insurance industry. The Contractor establishes catastrophe and coordination field offices in the event of large scale or severe flooding. These offices are set up to expedite claims and coordinate WYO activities. Also, through a central office and field offices, the Contractor supports NFIP outreach through coordination with FEMA's Regional Offices. The work that the Contractor will perform will be UNCLASSIFIED. It should be noted that a substantial amount of data is considered Personally Identifiable Information (PII) and must be treated as such.

CONSTRAINTS
The NFIP's SOR is both distributed and mainframe based with web based access and reporting, and it has been the NFIP's SOR for over 30 years. The Contractor shall operate and maintain the NFIP's SOR as it is currently configured, described and defined in this SOW. All data, licensed software, hand coded software and ancillary systems are owned by FEMA and are transferable to subsequent NFIP contractors.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 14

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support The Contractor shall not be inhibited from using software and other related materials which it has developed prior to this contract for its own management tools and for which it retains exclusive proprietary rights. However, such use is subject to prior approval by FEMA and any modifications to these materials that are required to make them applicable to and useable by the SOR shall not be undertaken as direct cost of this contract without prior authorization of the Contracting Officer (CO). Said authorization may, at the election of FEMA, also require license or sale to FEMA of the modified software at an agreed upon price.

APPLICABLE DOCUMENTS
SYNOPSIS: This SOW and other documents such as manuals, technical bulletins, brochures and other publications referenced in the SOW are provided in the Bidders Library. The location of this library will be provided by the CO. The Department of Homeland Security Sensitive Systems Policy Directive 4300A (DHS 4300A) is the official document relating to Departmental standards and guidelines adopted and promulgated under the provisions of DHS Management Directive 140-01 (MD 140-01) Information Technology System Security. MD 140-01 serves as a foundation for DHS organizational elements to use in establishing IT security programs within their organizations and clarifies national policies, adapts them to specific circumstances, and imposes additional requirements when necessary. DHS 4300A identifies procedures for implementing all applicable policies. DHS policies: DHS 4300A policies delineate the security management structure and foundation to measure progress and compliance. Policies in DHS 4300A document are organized under three areas, management, operational, and technical. Management Controls ­ Focus on managing both the IT security system and system risk. These controls consist of risk mitigation techniques and concerns normally addressed by management. Operational Controls ­ Focus on mechanisms primarily implemented and executed by people. These controls are designed to improve the security of a particular system, or group of systems. These controls require technical or specialized expertise and often rely on management and technical controls. Technical Controls ­ Focus on security controls executed by IT systems. These controls provide automated protection from unauthorized access or misuse. They facilitate detection of security violations, and support security requirements for applications and data. The Contractor is responsible for the implementation of the policies articulated in DHS 4300A and is required to inform the COR of any deviation from the policies stated therein. Such communication does not release the Contractor of any of its responsibilities as described within the SOW. PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 15

SOW OVERVIEW AND GENERAL COMMENTS
SYNOPSIS: This overview is intended to provide a summary look at the SOW. Specifically, Sections 1-40 provide details for the major functions that need to be provided by the Contractor. Where applicable, these sections contain tables that further define the support requirements for that section. Section 42 contains a comprehensive set of tables each of which provides a detailed list of functions that further define the specific task elements required by the Contractor. It is left to the Contractor to establish the appropriate correlation between Sections 1-40 and the tables in Section 43. BIGGERT-WATERS FLOOD INSURANCE REFORM AND MODERNIZATION ACT OF 2012 AND HOMEOWNER FLOOD INSURANCE AFFORDABILITY ACT OF 2014: The Biggert-Waters Flood Insurance Reform and Modernization Act of 2012 (BW-12) had two (2) major purposes. First, it reauthorized the NFIP for a five (5) year period that ends on September 30, 2017. Second, it provided for significant changes in the structure of the NFIP over this five (5) year period. The Homeowner Flood Insurance Affordability Act repeals and modifies certain provision of the Biggert-Waters Flood Insurance Reform Act but continues to work toward financial stability for the NFIP while also considering affordability for policyholders. Both acts make significant program changes of which the contractor must be aware and ready to implement FEMA-directed changes. The importance of these acts with respect to this SOW is that the Contractor will need to take into account that these structural modifications will have potentially significant impacts in terms of changes to existing requirements in this SOW as well as entirely new requirements that are not reflected in this SOW. In some cases, the NFIP is still analyzing requirements and working with internal and external stakeholders to develop implementation plans. This information is provided to identify for the Contractor that there will be changes to the scope of work over the period of performance. The changes that have been implemented by the award date or other such date as determined by FEMA are included in this SOW.

1.0

PROJECT MANAGEMENT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide experienced staff to manage the operations, maintenance and sustainment of the SOR. FEMA requires appropriate certification as described below and expects that these resources will be used to guide and direct the operations, maintenance and sustainment of the SOR in addition to transition activities, preparation of required documentation and quality assurance reviews. 1.1 EXPERIENCED PERSONNEL: The Contractor shall furnish staff with knowledge of the NFIP and a minimum of two years program management experience to research, analyze and make recommendations concerning the direction and conduct of the NFIP and support FEMA's response to case by case inquiries related to the items listed in the Table of Contents (SOW paragraphs 1-41). The Contractor shall supply suitably trained and experienced personnel needed to manage the operation and maintenance of the existing SOR who shall coordinate with the COR to ensure that FEMA priorities are met and managed. The Contractor shall coordinate with the FEMA Information System Security Manager (ISSM) as required to meet DHS and FEMA auditability, compliance, privacy and security requirements. Project and program management practices and reporting shall be implemented and monitored by Information Technology Infrastructure Library (ITIL) or Project Management Institute (PMI) Project Management Professional (PMP) certified personnel.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 19

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 1.2 SYSTEM OF RECORD OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE STANDARDS: The Contractor shall manage the operation and maintenance of the SOR to support FEMA, DSA and WYO stakeholders in a manner that would meet a Software Engineering Institute (SEI) Capability Maturity Model ­ Integrated (CMMI) Level 3 standards. The SOR and all of its related data is known as the Transaction Record Reporting and Processing (TRRP) which is also the financial management system for the NFIP, and includes all aspects of the program including, historical NFIP policy and claims information, actuarial data, claims processing, underwriting, and financial management reporting, analysis and assistance to FEMA. 1.3 QUARTERLY REVIEW: The Contractor shall conduct for FEMA a quarterly review of its staffing levels and operating costs, and present its findings to FEMA. Cost management, project budgeting, and project financial reporting shall be included in the analysis and application, as well as the implementation of relevant benchmarks and best practices. The Contractor shall conduct this review to assure FEMA's understanding of any and all issues that are pertinent. The Contractor shall present detailed supporting documentation for all invoices submitted for payment and explain deviations from forecasted expense level, for Cost Contract Line Items Only. 1.4 QUALITY CONTROL: Quality Control is the monitoring and oversight performed by the Contractor to ensure that work is accomplished in accordance with the terms of the contract. FEMA performs Quality Assurance to verify that the Contractor is performing the work required by the contract. The Contractor shall provide services in accordance with the terms of this contract. The Contractor shall develop a Quality Control Plan, which includes the following elements listed in Table 4.

2.0

BIGGERT-WATERS FLOOD INSURANCE REFORM AND MODERNIZATION ACT OF 2012 AND HOMEOWNER FLOOD INSURANCE AFFORDABILITY ACT OF 2014

SYNOPSIS: The U.S. Congress established the NFIP on August 1, 1968, with the passage of the National Flood Insurance Act (NFIA). The program was subsequently modified by other legislative measures such as the Flood Disaster Protection Act of 1973, the National Flood Insurance Reform Act (NFIRA) of 1994, and the Flood Insurance Reform Act (FIRA) of 2004. More recently, Congress passed significant flood insurance reform legislation on June 29, 2012, the Biggert-Waters Flood Insurance Reform and Modernization Act of 2012 (BW-12), which reauthorized the National Flood Insurance Program for a five year period that ends on September 30, 2017 and improved the financial underpinnings of the program. In 2014, Congress passed the Homeowner Flood Insurance Affordability Act (HFIAA) to work toward financial stability for the NFIP while also considering affordability for policyholders. The NFIP's current authorization to operate expires in 2017, and it can be assumed that requests for data and information about the program will increase during the Congressional reauthorization process before that time. The regulations governing the NFIP are set forth in Title 44 of the Code of Federal Regulations, Chapter I, Subchapter B, commencing at Part 59. The authority for the WYO Program as set forth in 44 CFR Parts 61 and 62, Sections 61.13 and 62.63. Appendix B to Part 62 establishes A Plan to Maintain Financial Control for Business Written Under the Write Your Own Program (Financial Control Plan). BW-12 and HFIAA included changes to address shortfalls in the NFIP's financing that required insurance rate increases and the collection of monies for a Reserve Fund, the result being that policyholders are being asked to pay more for their flood insurance. Needless to say, the higher rates have raised the visibility of the NFIP's insurance program, made the program the subject of media headlines across the country, and increased Congressional scrutiny of the program. More than ever in the NFIP's history there is a strong need for streamlined contractor support to assist FEMA with the 2012 and 2014 legislation, provisions of which will require many years to implement. Most importantly the NFIP's PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 21

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support national visibility, which has increased since the enactment of BW-12 and HFIAA, has reinforced the need for seamless contractor operational support. Both pieces of legislation will impact National Flood Insurance Program operations. BW-12 alone has forty (40) provisions including numerous studies which will fundamentally change the operations of the NFIP. Areas of particular impact are in Table 5

BW Key Provisions and Studies






  

Affordability Study -- depending on the outcome, FEMA could be required to means test for premium assistance; this testing will need the support of the Contractor and will require coordination with WYO companies. Alternative Loss Allocation -- the program will require a methodology to determine what percentage of a wind and water loss is attributed to wind damage compared to water damage. A centralized database could be required in order to issue the determination on a per claims basis. Flood in Progress -- which will require the contractor to notify the public in a timely manner as to when a flood has commenced or is in progress for the purposes of flood insurance coverage. Grandfathering, when implemented -- will require very specific property information in a single place to rate flood insurance policies Negative Elevation Rates -- the program will have to start collecting information and possibly maintain an elevation certificate database in order to properly rate structures since the pre-FIRM subsidy will be eliminated.

Table 5 BW Key Provisions and Studies

HFIAA requires gradual rate increases to properties receiving subsidized rates and individual premium increases are capped at 18 percent for most properties, with some exceptions. HFIAA repeals a provision of BW which required FEMA, upon the effective date of a new or updated Flood Insurance Rate Map, to phase in premium increases over five years by 20% per year. Rather HFIAA requires that these rates be phase in by 5 to 15 percent per year. The law also requires FEMA to prepare a draft affordability framework, including proposals for ensuring flood insurance affordability among low income populations. Table 6 lists the sections of both pieces of legislation that have an anticipated impact on the NFIP. The impact includes modifying business processes, modifying IT systems, doing analyses and providing communications.

3.0

UNDERWRITING SUPPORT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide underwriting support to FEMA, the WYO companies and the DSA contractor. This support involves providing technical assistance to these entities to ensure that each policy is correctly written and rated. 3.1 FLOOD INSURANCE UNDERWRITING KNOWLEDGE: The Contractor shall provide flood insurance underwriters with a minimum of three (3) years of experience underwriting flood insurance policies to respond to policyholders, FEMA, WYO companies, the DSA contractor, and other stakeholders in the implementation of the NFIP. The Contractor shall provide the following types of underwriting support shown in Table 7 on page 24.

Types of Underwriting Support
      Coordinating Coastal Barrier Resource Act (CBRA) eligibility with the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service Developing and updating the Flood Insurance Manual semi-annually per FEMA's revisions Gathering rating and payment information, calculating refunds, authorizing and initiating prior term refunds of premiums when applicable Providing technical assistance to WYO companies and the DSA contractor with applying the proper rules and regulations of the NFIP their books of business Reviewing and recommending approval of Preferred Risk Policy (PRP), CBRA Properties, Leased Federal Properties, 1316 Properties and Repetitive Loss Properties appeals for resolution by FEMA Supporting analysis, development and implementation of the requirements in the Biggert-Waters Flood Insurance Reform Act of 2012, Homeowners Flood Insurance Affordability Act 0f 2014 (HFIAA 2014) and NFIP Rate and Rule Changes

Table 7 Types of Underwriting Support

The Contractor shall receive, resolve, and track underwriting inquiries and coverage problems referred by FEMA, policy holders, agents, WYO Companies, State Insurance Departments, and others. For underwriting files where there is a question of coverage involving policy interpretation, the Contractor shall promptly refer them to FEMA through the COR. The Contractor has three (3) business days from the date of receipt to respond to a WYO company or DSA contractor inquiry or forward it to FEMA. The Contractor has three (3) business days from receiving FEMA's response to an inquiry to send it to the WYO Company or DSA contractor.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 24

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 3.2 COLLECTION OF INFORMATION: The Contractor shall collect and support the exchange of underwriting information between WYO companies, the DSA contractor, and FEMA. The Contractor shall develop and, with FEMA approval, disseminate underwriting bulletins concerning FEMA's decisions on underwriting issues. 3.3 SUBMIT FOR RATE: The Contractor shall support the Submit for Rate process. The Contractor shall secure Submit for Rate (SFR) files from WYO companies and the DSA contractor at FEMA's request; these files must be in hard copy, and all necessary documentation must be verified prior to submittal to FEMA. The Contractor shall review and verify that inquiries on new and existing policies are correctly rated and on buildings with the same property address. The Contractor shall follow up on pending new and existing policies. The Contractor shall daily validate the files for accuracy and completeness prior to forwarding the files to FEMA for review. The Contractor shall develop and update text, tables and graphics for the Specific Rating Guidelines every year. The Contractor shall address inquiries sent from FEMA on new inquiries and follow up on these inquiries.

4.0

CLAIMS SUPPORT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide support for claims processing to FEMA, the WYO companies and the DSA contractor. The support is required to ensure the proper collection of accurate claims information for all claims submitted. This entails providing general adjusters and managing their certifications, performing reinspections as necessary, process appeals as necessary, maintain appropriate logs, and perform special projects and analyses as requested. 4.1 FLOOD INSURANCE CLAIMS KNOWLEDGE: The Contractor shall provide experienced flood insurance claims personnel to respond to and support FEMA, the WYO companies, the DSA contractor and other stakeholders in the implementation of the NFIP claims program. The Contractor shall provide personnel with two different levels of claims experience. One level shall have, at minimum, one (1) year of experience in property insurance claims; the other level shall have, at a minimum, three (3) years of experience in commercial insurance claims. 4.2 COLLECTION OF CLAIMS INFORMATION: The Contractor shall be the focal point for the collection of information about coverage issues, policy interpretation, severity questions, and all other claims matters. If the issue is critical or time sensitive, the issue shall be referred to FEMA through the COR within 24 hours of determination of such. Otherwise, the Contractor shall process all claims information and subsequently notify FEMA of issues encountered and all actions taken by the Contractor. 4.3 WYO COMPANY AND DSA CONTRACTOR CLAIMS SUPPORT: The Contractor shall coordinate claims activities of WYO companies, the DSA contractor, and when appropriate, other Government agencies. The Contractor shall provide special assistance to the WYO Companies and the DSA contractor on claims issues. The Contractor shall provide coverage information, and other support, e.g., assist carriers on subrogation investigations, special assistance reinspections, provide policy and claim information, assist the Inspector General (IG) with investigations, attend regional meetings which may include federal, state or local government representation and maintain and prepare Special Allocated Loss Adjustment Expenses (SALAEs) for FEMA's review and approval. PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 25

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support The Contractor shall assist WYO companies and the DSA contractor in their claims adjustment process by responding to their requests for prior claims information. If the requested information is not available in the Actuarial Information System (AIS) system or Transaction Record Reporting Processing (TRRP), the Contractor shall gather the needed claims and underwriting information from WYO Companies or the DSA contractor and provide that information to the requesting WYO Company or DSA contractor holding the current policy. The Contractor shall only provide claims and other information to WYO companies, the DSA contractor, and others identified as FEMA Routine Users in the Federal Register pursuant to the Privacy Act.1

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 4.4 CLAIMS APPEALS SUPPORT: The Contractor shall support FEMA in the Claims Appeals process by reviewing and investigating losses through claim file reviews or reinspections. See additionally Section 6.0 CORREESPONDENCE SUPPORT. The Contractor shall provide support for Claims Appeals as required by FIRA, Section 205. 4.5 SUBROGATION LOG: The Contractor shall develop and maintain a subrogation log to include complete claim information, such as policyholder name, policy number, date of loss, WYO Company, subrogor, comments, etc. The Contractor shall obtain from WYO Companies or the DSA contractor as appropriate complete claims information, which may include requesting the file, and additional investigation by a qualified staff adjuster. The Contractor shall submit a quarterly report on subrogation activities to FEMA. 4.6 ASSIGNMENT OF INCREASED COST OF COMPLIANCE (ICC): The Contractor shall maintain a log of all claims reported where the policyholder consents to the assignment of the ICC claim payment. The Contractor shall obtain a copy of the Assignment of Increased Cost of Compliance, and supporting documentation to be disseminated to the appropriate WYO carrier or the DSA contractor. 4.7 SPECIAL CLAIMS PROJECTS AND ANALYSES: In response to inquiries from Congress, the Contractor shall assist the COR in conducting special claims projects and analyses. The projects may involve an in-depth review of claims files and field surveys of specifically identified areas (for example, condominiums, ICC, repetitive loss, subrogation, CBRA, high value properties, elevated buildings, basements, etc.). The Contractor shall also support other ad hoc claims analyses. 4.8 SPECIAL ALLOCATED LOSS ADJUSTMENT EXPENSES (SALAE): The Contractor shall receive from the WYO Companies and the DSA contractor all SALAE requests and review and submit them to FEMA for disposition, approval, disapproval, or requests for additional information. The Contractor shall provide space for up to two (2) FEMA staff on a weekly basis in the Contractors offices for FEMA staff to review SALAE requests and, once approved, the Contractor shall send approval letters to either the WYO Company or the DSA contractor over their (Contractor) signature. Biweekly, the Contractor shall provide detailed report on SALAE requests and approvals including named insured, date of loss, the style of the suit, defense attorneys, date of invoice, dollar amount of the invoice, status (approved, disapproved, additional information requested). FEMA must approve the format of this report.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 27

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 4.9 GENERAL ADJUSTER SUPPORT: The Contractor shall provide an in-house staff of no less than six (6) General Adjusters with NFIP flood insurance claims experience and have the capability to increase the numbers of General Adjusters needed to service any flood event. The NFIP General Adjusters are required to be claims professionals, have all applicable NFIP Flood Certifications, have appropriate NFIP flood insurance claims experience to expertly address difficult technical claims issues with policyholders and their representatives, and have the computer and software skills necessary to perform the duties. The Contractor shall provide General Adjusters with two (2) different types and levels of experience: some shall have a minimum of five (5) years of experience in residential flood claims estimating, and some shall have a minimum of five (5) years of experience in commercial estimating. The NFIP General Adjusters must demonstrate excellent customer service skills, and written and verbal communication skills. NFIP General Adjusters may be required to travel extensively in the USA, and the U.S. Territories, to conduct damage assessments, adjuster briefings and workshops to staff catastrophe offices in flooded areas, to conduct reinspections, and other assigned duties. 4.10 CLAIMS REINSPECTION: The Contractor shall plan, implement and manage the NFIP Claims Reinspection. There are three (3) types of reinspections: Congressional, FEMA Appeals and Special Assists. The major functions that the Contractor shall provide are listed in Table 8 below.

Major Functions for Claims Reinspections
  The Contractor is required to have NFIP certified General Adjusters make on-site property reinspections; one General Adjuster is required at each reinspection. The Contractor shall analyze and summarize the results of the reinspections, including identifying trends, overpayments and underpayments, etc. The Contractor shall provide a quarterly report on reinspection activities to FEMA. FEMA must approve the format of these reports. The Contractor shall maintain a detailed database of the reinspections and the associated findings. The Contractor shall provide feedback to FEMA, the WYO companies, and the DSA contractor through the COR on claims matters arising from reinspections, including repeated issues and trends. The Contractor shall support FEMA by reviewing and investigating losses through claim file reviews or reinspections.

4.11 TROUBLESHOOT PROBLEMS: The Contractor shall troubleshoot problems for FEMA, policyholders, WYO companies, DSA contractor, adjusters, and agents as they relate to specific flood claims by assigning the claim to a qualified General Adjuster for further investigation and disposition. The Contractor shall report the findings to FEMA, the WYO Company and the DSA contractor. 4.12 ADJUSTER CERTIFICATION MANAGEMENT: The Contractor shall transition in from the NFIP training contractor information (dates, names, etc.) regarding adjusters seeking NFIP certification or annual recertification. The Contractor shall use this information to track the adjuster training, which is a prerequisite for NFIP certification and recertification, distribute adjuster certification documentation with flood control numbers, and maintain historical records. 4.13 DAILY FLOOD EVENTS REPORT: The Contractor shall monitor daily weather conditions and send a report of current flooding events to FEMA by 8:30 AM EST daily.

5.0

FLOOD DISASTER RESPONSE SUPPORT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide support in establishing and maintaining Flood Response Offices (FROs) as described below. These offices are required when there is a flood event that FEMA needs to respond to in order appropriately and effectively deliver services directly into an affected area. 5.1 ACTIVATE FLOOD RESPONSE OFFICES: At any time, FEMA may, at its option and upon notice to the Contractor in accordance with the provisions of this section, require the Contractor to activate and operate one or more FROs for any duration. FEMA shall provide the Contractor written, electronic or telephonic notice of exercise of the option specified hereinabove. In the event notice is given by telephone, written or electronic confirmation shall be provided. Such notice shall specify the time at which the period of Flood Disaster Response (FDR) is to commence, which shall not be less than twenty four (24) hours subsequent to the receipt of such notice by the Contractor or his representative, or shall be a later time at which the FRO disaster team or teams can reasonably arrive at a safe location at which an FRO can be established and maintained and remain there for the anticipated duration of the FDR period. FEMA shall provide the Contractor written, electronic or verbal notice within a reasonable period of time (in the event notice is given by telephone, written or electronic confirmation shall be provided) of termination of the period of FDR.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 29

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 5.2 REIMBURSEMENT OF FRO EXPENSES: FEMA shall reimburse the Contractor for reimbursable supplies and services are those items specified in the contract as reimbursable, or otherwise preapproved by the CO. 5.3 DISASTER DAILY SITUATION REPORT: In the event of a flood disaster, the Daily Situation Report shall both contain information from NFIP General Adjusters and Contractor staff deployed in the disaster area and be delivered by 8:30 AM EST (EDST) each day. This report shall assess the extent of the damage caused by flooding including any information to be used by FEMA to develop a Probable Maximum Loss (PML), including frequency and severity. This information should be used to support the Contractor's advice to FEMA of the need to establish field offices. 5.4 FLOOD INSURANCE CLAIMS OFFICE NUMBER: The Contractor shall advise FEMA that a Flood Insurance Claims Office (FICO) number is required to track all ensuing claims of severe flooding events. At the direction of FEMA, the Contractor shall disseminate a claims bulletin to the WYO Principal Coordinators and the DSA contractor advising of the FICO number(s), affected states, and the dates of loss. 5.5 DAILY CLAIMS POLLING: The Contractor shall establish a daily report of claims reported by WYO Companies or the DSA contractor. The report should capture all claims reporting activity for the event, such as total losses reported by WYO Company, advance payments on claims, dollars paid when closed, total paid, average claim paid, etc. The Contractor shall notify the appropriate WYO Companies or the DSA contractor via email to begin the polling process, which includes the dates of loss, FICO number, and affected state(s). The Contractor shall receive and validate statistical claims data, compile reports and disseminate information to FEMA daily by 9:30 AM EST (EDST). The Contractor shall track the performance of the WYO companies and the DSA contractor and report discrepancies to FEMA. FEMA shall approve the format of this report. 5.6 FLOOD RESPONSE OFFICES: At the time of a flood disaster, the COR will direct the Contractor to establish, administer, and operate one or more Flood Response Offices (FROs) to promote and assist WYO Companies and the DSA contractor with coverage issues, and other services, such as reinspections, to assure the timely, fair, and efficient adjustment and settlement of NFIP claims. In the event of a flooding event, the Contractor shall provide qualified, NFIP certified adjusters to augment the existing General Adjusters. The Contractor shall submit a plan to provide additional qualified, NFIP certified adjusters to the COR for approval prior to May 1st of each year. This is thirty one (31) calendar days prior to the beginning of hurricane season which commences on June 1st of each year. The Contractor shall prepare to deploy, within twenty four (24) hours of notice by the COR, no fewer than six (6) FRO disaster teams, which include, when appropriate, persons fluent in Spanish. Each team PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 30

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support shall be prepared to establish a FRO and begin operations along with WYO Companies and others in the flooded areas within seven (7) calendar days of notification by the COR. The Contractor shall also be prepared to fill, within seven (7) calendar days of notice, an additional back-up team or teams to conduct FRO activities, in the event of six (6) or more geographically distant but simultaneous flood disasters. The Contractor shall provide adequate office space for each FRO; this is subject to approval from the COR. The Contractor shall inform the involved FEMA region or regions of the location of each FRO that is established. 5.7 FLOOD RESPONSE OFFICES ACTIVITIES: The Contractor's FRO activities provide an NFIP local presence to conduct adjuster and agent claims briefings, support WYO Companies and the DSA contractor, contact field agents, conduct on-site claims surveys and reinspections, and disseminate forms and information as needed. The Contractor shall, in keeping with FEMA guidelines, perform and coordinate with other Government operations. The Contractor shall assist the WYO Companies and the DSA contractor by providing guidance, information about the certification of individual adjusters in affected areas, and other flood disaster coordination activities. The FROs shall serve as on-site emergency supply centers for NFIP forms, Standard Flood Insurance Policies, bulletins, printed supplies and other information to expedite NFIP excellent customer service and claims handling. Examples of these documents are provided in the Bidders Library. The Contractor shall establish the telephone, network and computer resources necessary to support business activities in the field for flood response personnel that need to be on-site to assist the Contractor and other field operations. 5.8 COLLABORATION WITH OTHER NFIP STAKEHOLDERS: The Contractor shall develop procedures, guidelines, and other needed materials to facilitate coordination among WYO Companies and the DSA contractor in the event of catastrophic flooding. The Contractor shall participate in collaboration activities between the WYO Companies and the DSA contractor with the FRO as well as with any other Government disaster assistance activities as approved by the COR. FEMA anticipates such collaboration to be as shown in Table 9 below.

Stakeholder Collaboration Activities

6.0

CORRESPONDENCE SUPPORT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide support for the correspondence that is required to meet stakeholder needs. This support consists of establishing documented procedures for handling all correspondence, fielding the originating requests, creating appropriate responses for the request and maintaining logs of all correspondence activity. The Risk Insurance Division currently uses the following definitions in its correspondence process: controlled correspondence originates from the Department of Homeland Security (DHS), the White House, and Congress; claims appeals correspondence is simply a claim appeal; and uncontrolled correspondence is anything not included in the previous categories (controlled or claims appeals). 6.1 CORRESPONDENCE: The Contractor shall respond to technical claims and underwriting inquiries and review the grammar and technical content of the draft responses prior to forwarding them to FEMA. The Contractor shall use FEMA approved templates developed in InfoPath of sample letters as guides in formatting a draft response letter. The Contractor shall be prepared to work with Microsoft technologies, for example InfoPath and SharePoint. Draft responses should be ready for delivery to the stakeholders when sent to FEMA. It is vital that draft responses have no spelling, grammatical, or punctuation errors and are precise, concise and reflect agency values, clear writing and exemplary customer service. FEMA will mail the final letters to the WYO Company and DSA contractor points of contact. The objectives for correspondence follow in Table 10.

Correspondence Support Activities
    All acknowledgement letters or other interim communications shall include a telephone number provided by the Contractor for inquiries regarding correspondence. Appeal Correspondence: a finalized copy to FEMA, within forty five (45) business days, with an acknowledgement letter sent within two business days of receipt of initial inquiry. Claims Controlled Correspondence: a finalized copy FEMA, within five (5) business days from date of receipt, with an acknowledgement letter sent within one business day of receipt off initial inquiry. The Contractor shall respond to inquiries regarding the status of correspondence in writing or by telephone.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 32

Correspondence Support Activities
   Uncontrolled Correspondence: a finalized copy to FEMA, within thirty (20) business days from date of receipt Underwriting Controlled Correspondence: a finalized copy to FEMA, within five (5) business days from date of receipt, with an acknowledgement letter sent within one business day of receipt of initial inquiry. VIP Correspondence ­ Formal communications between FEMA, DHS, Congress, The White House, governors and others is closely monitored and is categorized internally as Controlled Correspondence. Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 6.2 CORRESPONDENCE PROCEDURES: The Contractor shall implement, document, and maintain detailed procedures for handling of all NFIP related correspondence. FEMA shall approve these procedures as per the note on the Deliverables Chart. Procedures shall evidence the ability to provide complete control over all incoming and outgoing correspondence, perform quality assurance, and timely performance of all correspondence tasks. 6.3 CORRESPONDENCE TRACKING: The Contractor shall operate an automated system for the control and analysis of all correspondence received to include a diary system that ensures accurate and efficient data capture processing during the life cycle of the claim correspondence, e.g. notifications of incoming correspondence, notification of all activity, track correspondence status, etc. The tracking system shall, at a minimum, provide reports on the nature of correspondence, sources, (such as White House, Congress, State Officials, agent, insured, etc.) trends (such as geographic, programmatic) and timeliness of problem resolution, and replies to correspondence. The Contractor shall have the ability to upload and electronically deliver to FEMA complete files that are too large to send via email. The Contractor should be prepared to accommodate correspondence procedural changes due to significant disasters, changes to internal FEMA correspondence processes or other issues.

FIELD OFFICE SUPPORT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall establish and provide support for each of the ten (10) FEMA Regional Offices in order to support Regional Insurance Specialists by developing and implementing outreach activities, assisting with community and policy holder issues, and responding to flood events at the direction of the COR. 7.1 REGIONAL FIELD OFFICES: The Contractor shall establish regional field offices within the first six (6) months of performance to support the NFIP and the ten (10) FEMA Regional Offices using policy counts and insurance exposure as guidelines. 7.2 REGIONAL ACTIVITIES: The Contractor shall perform the representative field office activities enumerated below and coordinate their activities with the FEMA Regional Offices and the COR. A monthly report which summarizes the monthly activities of the regional personnel is included in the deliverables list. 8.0

FORMS, MANUALS AND PUBLICATIONS

SYNOPSIS: The forms, manuals and publications objectives shall be done in coordination with FEMA's Printing Officer, Forms Management Officer, and Information Officers, and consistent with their guidance. These objectives should also be consistent with the Paperwork Reduction Act of 1995, and implementing OMB Regulation 5 C.F.R 1320, the Joint Committee on Printing Regulations, and Government Printing Office regulations. 8.1 DEVELOP AND MAINTAIN: The Contractor shall develop and maintain operating forms, manuals and other required publication, including bilingual materials in accordance with all applicable Government regulations. Development and changes to the forms shall be coordinated with FEMA, to include the COR. Examples of these documents are provided in the Bidders Library. 8.2 DESCRIPTIVE MATERIALS: At the direction of the COR, the Contractor shall develop and supply descriptive, paper-based materials and program information (brochures, information Fact Sheets, FAQs, etc.) It is vital that draft materials have no spelling, grammatical, or punctuation errors and are precise, concise and reflect agency values, clear writing and exemplary professionalism. Some materials developed require significant concurrence from many program offices within FEMA and may require multiple revisions. Timelines for delivery should include extra time to accommodate significant reviews. The Contractor shall review and obtain all necessary approvals in writing from all those identified by the COR, prior to sending the materials to the FEMA printer for printing and prior to releasing any materials. For printed materials, the Contractor shall produce the materials up to the point of printing, including the design, technical writing, and graphics design and must adhere to FEMA, DHS and GPO guidelines and regulations. All materials shall meet the highest professional production standards. FEMA approved descriptive materials and program information may be distributed as copies or as reproducible masters or electronically to requesting stakeholders.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 36

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 8.3 PRODUCTION: The Contractor shall be responsible for production, including the design, technical writing, graphics, obtaining printing authorization, printing and distribution.

9.0

PUBLICATION AND DOCUMENT ASSISTANCE

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall develop, edit and ensure the quality of materials necessary to support the NFIP. The materials should be delivered to the COR ready to be published, after the Contractor has performed a thorough quality check on both the grammar and technical aspects of the document. It is vital that draft materials have no spelling, grammatical, or punctuation, errors, and are precise, concise and reflect agency values, clear writing and exemplary professionalism. Some materials developed require significant concurrence from many program offices within FEMA and may require multiple revisions. Timelines for delivery should include extra time to accommodate significant reviews. The Contractor shall review and obtain all necessary approvals in writing from all those identified by the COR or his/her designee, prior to sending the materials to the FEMA printer for printing and prior to releasing any materials. The Contractor shall provide one Communications manager with at least five (5) years relevant experience in communications management or document creation/publishing and at least one writer with a minimum of two (2) years of relevant experience in technical writing and materials development or production. The responsibilities for publication and document support shall include the items in Table 12.

10.0 PROGRAM SUPPORT AND REPORTING
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide program support and miscellaneous reporting as described below to facilitate effective program management. These functions are necessary to provide transparency of operations, documentation of key rate and table information, and assist stakeholders with information that they may need. The Contractor is expected to provide overall support as defined in this SOW to the NFIP and its stakeholders as may be required by disaster or business events during non-business hours. 10.1 DOCUMENTATION: The Contractor shall develop, maintain, and revise, as required, the rate tables and rate keys, TRRP Plan documentation, and the methodology for calculating earned premium, unearned premium, deferred acquisition costs, and loss and loss adjustment reserves. 10.2 TECHNICAL REPORTS: The Contractor shall effectively manage, produce and quality control the timely production of reports in support of Program development and other activities, including regularly scheduled, ad hoc, special automated and non-automated reports. Within two (2) business days of a request by the COR, the Contractor shall deliver technical report designs identifying source data and calculations performed within report.

11.0 DOCUMENT CLEARINGHOUSE
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall be responsible for developing and maintaining bulletins, newsletters and other communications as designated by FEMA. In doing so, the Contractor shall maintain adequate records and inventories and monitor all materials for timeliness, accuracy and quality; where issues with any of these are identified, the Contractor shall inform the COR of the issues. 11.1 ESTABLISH AND MAINTAIN: The Contractor shall establish and maintain a list of electronic and other mailings in support of the NFIP. The list should include current and historical information. The Contractor shall establish and maintain a document clearinghouse for the development and distribution of materials and publications. The types of material to be developed and maintained by the clearinghouse include bulletins, newsletters and other communications as designated by FEMA. 11.2 ADEQUATE RECORDS AND INVENTORIES: The Contractor shall maintain adequate records and inventories of printed NFIP and WYO materials, which include newsletters, bulletins, and the claims manual. The Contractor shall provide sufficient and appropriate warehouse space to maintain form and historical document inventories. The warehouse is used to store historical business records, equipment needed for FROs (technology kits and other physical assets), FIRA Mail, and FEMA Publications. 11.3 ACCURACY AND QUALITY: The Contractor shall monitor and assure the informational and editorial accuracy of program materials supplied to NFIP stakeholders. See eWATERMARK SUPPORT below. Recent legislation has driven a number of programmatic changes in the NFIP, rendering some existing publications obsolete. If issues with timeliness, quality or accuracy are identified, the Contractor shall inform the COR of issues.

12.0 eWATERMARK SUPPORT
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall assist in the creation, writing, design, editing, publication and distribution for a periodically produced (periodicity is shown below) electronic newsletter. 12.1 EDITORIAL SUPPORT AND ASSISTANCE: The Contractor shall provide personnel with knowledge of the NFIP to support and assist the FEMA editor of that newsletter, including writing and editing several articles about events in areas within their expertise Some examples are, the FEMA semiannual rate and rule changes (one to two articles yearly), reporting on the annual National Flood Conference in articles about the conference activities, award winners and related activities (two to three articles yearly), and any other areas for which they may be responsible (such as underwriting, claims, and related activities, if these are within their expertise). 12.2 eWATERMARK EDITOR: The Contractor shall designate a Supporting Editor, who has a minimum of two (2) years of experience in creating, writing, designing, editing, publishing and distributing electronic publications on a routine schedule and who will assist the FEMA editor with preparing eWatermark articles provided by FEMA. The newsletter shall be updated several times a year, not more often than once a month. It is vital that draft newsletters have no spelling, grammatical, or punctuation errors, and are precise, concise and reflect agency values, clear writing and exemplary professionalism. 13.0 WEBSITE SUPPORT
SYNOPSIS: The IT architecture for all websites implemented must be consistent with the FEMA Enterprise Architecture. In addition, any IT systems used to collect FEMA data in the performance of this contract shall meet all applicable DHS and FEMA security requirements and be certified and accredited, as required, in coordination with the FEMA Office of the Chief Information Officer (OCIO), unless otherwise waived by an authorized FEMA official. 13.1 WEBSITE DEVELOPMENT: The Contractor shall consolidate pertinent data contained within www.nfipiservice.com and bsa.nfipstat.fema.gov into a single website supporting the NFIP by providing information for public stakeholders, which shall be ready to go live at the end of the transition period (See TRANSITION-IN AND TRANSITION-OUT SERVICES). It is currently anticipated that the site could be further consolidated as directed by the FEMA Office of External Affairs. The combined NFIP website will disseminate information such as bulletins, forms for claims, training dates, the eWatermark newsletter, etc. This website shall have links available to historic articles and various subpages. Currently the two sites are not part of the fema.gov web enterprise which is operated and maintained by FEMA's Office of External Affairs. If those sites do become part of the FEMA.gov system, additional Government rules and guidelines will apply. 13.2 WEBSITE MANAGEMENT AND MAINTENANCE: The Contractor shall ensure continuous functioning of the new website after the transition. The Contractor shall provide all services necessary to enhance and update the website. The Contractor shall maintain and make appropriate changes to the content, provide account management, strategic consulting, project management and site hosting. Under the direction of the COR, the Contractor shall also create, update and maintain resource library records for NFIP materials located at www.fema.gov/national-flood-insurance-program. Additionally, the Contractor shall review the resource library for redundancies and outdated materials. 13.3 WEBSITE HOSTING The Contractor shall host the FloodSmart marketing websites and the Underwriting-Claims Operation Review Tool (UCORT). The Contractor shall provide requested data sets per company (either WYO or DSA) as requested by FEMA to support the UCORT system.

14.0 COMMUNICATION TO POLICYHOLDERS UNDER FLOOD INSURANCE REFORM ACT of 2004 and HOMEOWNER FLOOD INSURANCE AFFORDABILITY ACT of 2014 SYNOPSIS
SYNOPSIS: FEMA is required to implement the Title II requirements of the Flood Insurance Reform Act (FIRA) of 2004 and Section 28 of the Homeowner Flood Insurance Affordability Act of 2014 (HFIAA). 14.1 MAILINGS: The Contractor shall send with each new policy and additionally at each annual renewal, the property's loss history information, as required by FIRA, Section 202 (a)(4), the Claims Handbook, as required by FIRA, Section 204, the acknowledgment, as required by FIRA, Section 203, and a cover letter that references these enclosures. The Contractor shall also include the true flood risk determination of property regardless of the premium being charged, as required by HFIAA Section 28. The volume of mailings is approximately six (6) million per year. 14.2 RECORD KEEPING: The Contractor shall implement and maintain electronic record-keeping procedures for the acknowledgement letter to show proof of mailing and receipt or lack of receipt of a policyholder's signed acknowledgement. The volume of acknowledgements is approximately 2.5 million per year.

The Contractor shall develop a FEMA approved SOP for such activities, and shall, as appropriate, recommend changes to the SOP and to FEMA Records Disposition Schedule as appropriate. The media used for record keeping must be in compliance with the Federal Records Act, National Archives and Records Administration regulations, and guidance provided by the FEMA Records Officer. 15.2 SCANNING: The Contractor shall scan the documents detailed below and make the scanned copies available to FEMA personnel upon request. 16.0 MEETINGS AND CONFERENCES
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall plan and coordinate the numerous conferences and committee meetings described below. These conferences and meetings are a key part of the NFIP 's outreach and communication efforts as well as a means to solicit industry input. 16.1 NATIONAL FLOOD CONFERENCE: As directed by the COR, the Contractor shall support the planning and coordination of the National Flood Conference (NFC) with the COR and FEMA planning representatives. The Contractor shall provide expert conference planning experience to assist in planning the NFC; the conference planner shall have at least three years of experience planning large conferences with 500 to 1,000 attendees. The Conference Planner must adhere to all Government regulations including Government Services Agency (GSA) and Office of Management and Budget (OMB) rules and regulations, Section 508 accessibility, ADA Accessibility, contracting law and other applicable regulations. Contractor must demonstrate knowledge of government rules and/or experience planning government conferences. Contractor must meticulously track all government expenditures and maintain detailed budgets at all phases of conference planning. 16.2 MEETINGS: The Contractor shall participate at and assist in non-training and non-media activities, with the approval of the COR. These activities can include meetings with groups (agents, lenders, Government officials, and citizens); independent claims adjustment organizations, WYO companies, etc. The Contractor shall, having been provided reasonable notice, participate in meetings, conferences, conventions, and trade shows, including those that may include WYO companies, FEMA contractors, NFIP stakeholders or combinations thereof. The Contractor shall prepare and supply materials to facilitate communication of NFIP information to these audiences. 17.0 POSTAGE, FREIGHT AND DELIVERY
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide all mailroom courier functions to support communications with FEMA and the various NFIP Stakeholders and in support of the FIRA of 2004. 17.1 MANAGEMENT CONTROL: The Contractor shall establish and maintain internal controls to assure the security and accounting for all postage, private express delivery, freight, and delivery expenses of the program. The Contractor shall manage postage and express delivery activities to minimize costs to FEMA. 17.2 MANAGEMENT CONTROL: The Contractor shall report monthly on the nature of postal and express delivery expenditures, any unusual or unanticipated expenses, measures being taken and progress being made to reduce the costs. The Contractor shall make best efforts to reduce postage, freight and delivery costs by, for example, preparing mailing lists annually, using the most economic classes of mail, and using all applicable US Postal Service discounts. 17.3 LETTER OF CREDIT: All costs for postage, private express delivery, freight, and delivery shall be paid directly out of a Letter of Credit in accordance with the procedures for use of a Letter of Credit. No fee will be paid on postage, freight or delivery expenses. 17.4 COURIER: The Contractor shall provide a daily courier drop off and pick up at FEMA's Crystal City (Arlington, VA) facility. The courier shall meet all Federal, DHS, and FEMA security badging and clearance requirements to facilitate services.

18.0 ACCOUNTING AND FINANCIAL CONTROL SUPPORT
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall perform all accounting and financial control functions described below to ensure the financial integrity of the program. FEMA is responsible for both maintaining accurate financial records and reporting relevant financial information to DHS. 18.1 COMPREHENSIVE ACCOUNTING SYSTEM: The Contractor shall be responsible for the operation and maintenance of a comprehensive accounting system for the NFIP and for the financial aspects of the WYO Financial Control Plan. The accounting system shall support the requirements of the Chief Financial Officers Act of 1990, the financial controls of OMB Bulletin #1-09, and the preparation of consolidated financial statements and reports. The system shall support information needs for effective cash management and control of Federal funds. 18.2 CASH RECEIPTS AND DISBURSEMENTS: The Contractor shall provide in accordance with Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) cash receipts and disbursements and perform a monthly reconciliation of all receipts and disbursements. The Contractor shall provide adequate generally accepted internal controls for cash receipts and disbursements and establish internal control to safeguard Government funds and interest.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 45

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 18.3 MAINTAIN AN AUTOMATED GENERAL LEDGER: The Contractor shall maintain an automated general ledger (G/L) on an accrual basis in conformance with GAAP. Conversely, the Contractor shall exchange financial information via an automated interface with the FEMA accounting system and Integrated Financial Management Information System (IFMIS) that requires U.S. Government Standard General Ledger accounts format as documented in the Treasury Financial Manual. 18.4 RECONCILIATION OF GENERAL LEDGER: The Contractor shall perform the reconciliation of G/L accounts and adjustment of entries on a monthly basis. The Contractor shall, on a monthly basis, reconcile G/L accounts to supporting records (TRRP Plan submissions, adjustments, financial reconciliation, etc.) to validate accruals of income and expenses. 18.5 DETAILED AUDIT TRAIL: The Contractor shall maintain a detailed audit trail of all transactions, consistent with GAAP accounting methods. The audit data shall be sufficient in detail to facilitate the reconstruction of financial activity if compromise or malfunction occurs or is suspected. All manual G/L entries shall be separately verified and fully tracked. 18.6 REPORT AVAILABILITY: The Contractor shall make available online within two (2) business days after request by FEMA any financial reporting pertaining to current or historical reporting periods as may be required to meet FEMA reporting requirements. Financial records shall be maintained in accordance with FEMA Records Disposition Schedule. The media used for record keeping shall be in compliance with the Federal Records Act, National Archives and Records Administration regulations and guidance provided by the FEMA Records Officer. 18.7 ACCOUNTING REPORTS: The Contractor shall perform all accounting and financial control functions while maintaining and operating the SOR. There is a summary of the required documents in the Deliverables Chart at the end of this Statement of Work. The deliverables shall be delivered to the COR by the due date listed. The COR then has twenty (20) business days to review each report and request corrections from the Contractor before the document is accepted by FEMA. Once approved by FEMA, some of these reports shall be shared with other FEMA stakeholders. The current accounting reports and their timing of delivery are shown in Table 16 below.

20.0 STATISTICAL AND FINANCIAL REPORTING
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide accounting and financial management support to respond to the needs of FEMA, the WYO Companies, other contractor staff, auditors and other stakeholders in the operation of the WYO Program. Such support shall include the sustainment of automated systems for the communication, recording, and transfer of financial data; reviewing materials for program consistency; and if required, development and providing technical assistance to the WYO Companies. 20.1 EXPERIENCED FINANCIAL PERSONNEL: The Contractor shall supply suitably trained and experienced financial personnel needed to prepare, edit and analyze financial reports and statements. A minimum of one (1) licensed Certified Public Accountant must be provided. 20.2 REPORTING REQUIREMENTS: Reporting requirements shall be subjected to regular review for duplication and utility by the Contractor; all new reporting requests initiated by FEMA shall be examined to determine the most expeditious and economical manner in which to satisfy the requirements. These requirements shall apply to all reports, for WYO Companies and the DSA contractor's operations, including those reports generated for internal use by the Contractor as well as those provided FEMA and NFIP stakeholder use. 21.1 COMPREHENSIVE DATA COLLECTION: The Contractor shall maintain and operate a comprehensive data collection and reporting AIS, which encompasses all NFIP operations, including WYO Companies and the DSA contractor experience. Any changes done shall be in coordination with the COR. 21.2 AIS ANALYSES: The AIS shall be utilized for analyses of NFIP insurance experience on an accident year basis. Such analysis shall include: identifying past and present distribution of business; identifying, measuring and analyzing trends; providing data for input to rate setting models; and otherwise supporting the actuarial needs of the NFIP. 21.3 AIS ABILITY: The AIS shall provide the ability to develop insurance experience on the types of NFIP coverage for classifications and zones, distribution of business, distribution of claims and countrywide underwriting experience. The system shall allow for the capability to analyze underwriting experience in conjunction with geo-coded property information and digitized flood risk zone data. 21.4 REPORTING: A listing of all predefined reports is provided in the SYSTEM GENERATED MONTHLY, SEMI-ANNUAL AND ANNUAL REPORTS section 43.

22.0

ACTUARIAL SUPPORT

SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide expert actuarial support to perform reviews and analyses in support of FEMA's policy, financial, and rate setting responsibilities. 22.1 TRAINED AND EXPERIENCED PERSONNEL: The Contractor shall supply suitably trained and experienced actuarial personnel needed to assess and analyze business environments within which financial decisions concerning insurance and investments are made including the application of mathematical concepts and other techniques to the various areas of actuarial practice with a particular focus on flood insurance. The Contractor shall, at a minimum, retain the services of either an Associate (ACAS) or Fellow (FCAS) of the Casualty Actuarial Society (CAS) who is qualified to issue a Statement of Actuarial Opinion (SAO) regarding loss and loss expense reserves. 22.2 ACTUARIAL KNOWLEDGE: The Contractor shall provide expert actuarial and analytical support to respond to FEMA's needs in implementing and making policy decisions for the NFIP. 24.0 DHS ENTERPRISE ARCHITECTURE (EA) REQUIREMENTS
SYNOPSIS: All solutions and services shall meet DHS Enterprise Architecture policies, standards, and procedures. Specifically, the Contractor shall comply with the applicable DHS and FEMA requirements listed in Table 22. The Federal Enterprise Architecture (FEA)4 identifies the high level considerations that must be taken into account throughout the useful life of a system. The DHS/FEMA EA, security architecture, data management policy and related TRM have been developed as departmental and administration implementations of the FEA. All applicable policies apply to any modifications and upgrades to the NFIP IT legacy system that may occur prospectively and will be provided to the successful Offeror.

25.0 DISASTER RECOVERY AND CONTINUITY OF OPERATIONS
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall develop and maintain plans for Disaster Recovery (DR) and Continuity of Operations (COOP) to handle special and emergency circumstances which could jeopardize Contractor's support for the NFIP as described in this SOW. The Contractor shall provide an alternate processing facility to accomplish this. For purposes of this SOW, assume that all impacted environments must be available within 72 hours of a disaster declaration at the mainframe or distributed datacenter. This also applies to the Contractor's main processing center for NFIP support. 25.1 ANNUAL TESTING OF DISASTER RECOVERY: The Contractor shall develop and at least annually review, test, and update the Disaster Recovery and System Security Plans.
