26.1 INFORMATION SYSTEMS SECURITY OFFICER: The Information Systems Security Officer (ISSO) shall serve as the Point of Contact (POC) for all security matters related to the NFIP IT legacy system and shall ensure the implementation and maintenance of security controls in accordance with the Security Plan (SP) and DHS and FEMA policies. The Contractor shall provide a minimum of one (1) experienced ISSO who will work directly with the designated ISSM on all matters relating to auditability, compliance, privacy and security.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 57

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 26.2 SENSITIVE INFORMATION: The Contractor shall protect all DHS sensitive information to which the Contractor is granted physical or electronic access by adhering to the specific IT security requirements described within herein. 26.3 SECURITY REQUIREMENTS: The Contractor shall include security as an integral element in the management of this contract. The Contractor shall conduct reviews and report the status of the implementation and enforcement of the security requirements contained in this SOW and its related supporting documentation. Such reviews and reporting shall be conducted in accordance with the provisions of this document. The Contractor shall ensure that all individuals who perform activities in accordance with this SOW are U.S. citizens. The contractor shall follow established DHS and FEMA policies. 26.4 GOVERNMENT REVIEWS: The Government will conduct periodic reviews to ensure that the security requirements contained in this contract are being implemented and enforced. The Contractor shall afford DHS, including the Office of Inspector General and other Government oversight organizations, access to the Contractor and subcontractor's facilities, installations, operations, documentations, databases, and personnel used in the performance of this contract. Access shall be provided to the extent necessary for the Government to carry out its desired program of inspection, investigation, and audit to safeguard against threats and hazards to the integrity, availability, and confidentiality of its data or the function of computer systems operated on behalf of FEMA and to preserve evidence of computer crime. 26.5 AUTHORIZED PERSONNEL: The Contractor shall ensure that access to Contractor buildings, rooms, work areas, spaces, and structures that house DHS sensitive information or IT systems through which DHS sensitive information can be accessed, is limited to authorized personnel. The Contractor shall ensure that controls are implemented to deter, detect, monitor, restrict, and regulate access to controlled areas at all times. All Contractor personnel, subcontractors and consultants must be granted an "Entrance on Duty" by FEMA which requires US Citizenship and a favorable background investigation conducted by Government personnel, prior to being granted access to any Government owned machines or FEMA/NFIP systems. Access to any government owned equipment must meet specific safeguards that meet DHS 4300A policy which includes requiring approved two factor authentication in compliance with HSPD-12. 26.6 OPERATING PROCEDURES: The Contractor shall develop operating procedures to ensure that no dual responsibility roles are assigned that might compromise or circumvent the intent of FEMA's information systems security program. The Contractor shall maintain the procedures for currency and incorporate them into an overall System Security Plan. 26.7 RISK MANAGEMENT PLAN: The Contractor shall keep an up to date Risk Management Plan (RMP) including, at a minimum an annual test of the backup and recovery processes and procedures. Hardware failures, application software failures, and communication failures shall be fully corrected within the allowed downtime as stated within in this section.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 58

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 26.8 SECURITY AUTHORIZATION: The Contractor's systems facilities must meet all standards required by OMB Circular A-130 and the DHS 4300A. The Contractor shall develop a facility Security Plan and pursue a full Security Authorization to ensure protection and control of the sensitive, unclassified information maintained in the system. 26.9 DAILY BACK-UP: The Contractor shall, on a daily basis, perform backups of all files created or changed. All data and systems files over three (3) business days old shall be stored at an off-site location. All systems shall be fully documented and backed up each time they are changed and each week at a minimum. A complete system backup shall be conducted each weekend. Off-site storage shall meet the requirements for the long-term secure data storage of magnetic and optical media. The storage facility shall have the capability of delivering the backed up system to a pre-selected backup or alternate processing site within twenty four (24) hour notice. 26.10 OFF-SITE STORAGE LOCATION: Off-site storage shall meet business continuity objectives as described in DHS 4300A for the long-term secure data storage of magnetic and optical media. The storage facility shall have the capability of delivering the backed-up system to a pre-selected backup or alternate processing site within twenty four (24) hour notice. Restricted access to the back-up site shall be fully detailed in the Security Plan and be part of the Security Review. DHS FEMA Security Authorization activities shall verify that the Contractor has met storage requirements. 26.11 INCIDENT REPORT: The Contractor shall record and keep on file the complete history of all incidents reported and actions taken to handle the incident. All security incidents shall be reported to FEMA within twenty four (24) hours.

28.0 IT AUDIT SUPPORT
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall support all FEMA directed audits in all functional areas including the annual external fiscal year audit that covers the financial IT and security processes and procedures of the NFIP and which typically requires Contractor support throughout an nine (9) month period from March through November of each calendar year. 28.1 NFIP IT LEGACY SYSTEM AUDIT SUPPORT: The Contractor shall support the implementation of, and annual support for, all required audits. The Contractor shall support an annual IT System audit by a FEMA designated Audit contractor. This will require continuous Contractor support over the above noted audit period to include attending multiple meetings, providing support for on-site audit walkthroughs, providing auditable artifacts, responding to and remediating any Notice of Finding and Recommendation (NFR) that may be issued. The Contractor shall provide pre-audit support including meeting with a pre-audit contractor to prepare for the audit and participate in audit training.

29.0 BUSINESS AUDIT SUPPORT
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall support all FEMA directed audits in all functional areas including the annual external fiscal year audit that covers select aspects of the business processes described in this SOW which typically requires Contractor support throughout an nine (9) month period from March through November of each calendar year. 29.1 AUDIT AND WYO FCP ACTIVITIES SUPPORT: The Contractor shall support the implementation of, and annual support for FEMA's Financial Statement Audit, Improper Payments Elimination and Recovery Information Act of 2002 (IPERIA) audit, and WYO Financial Control Plan activities. 29.2 INTERNAL AUDIT: The Contractor shall establish internal audit activities for underwriting and claims analyses to assure the integrity of WYO underwriting and claims data and reporting.

This includes configuration change identification, configuration control, configuration status accounting, and the support of configuration audits. FEMA maintains its right to perform a CM Audit once every year during the contract period of performance. The Contractor shall receive audit criteria guidelines in advance of a CM audit. The audit shall assess the Contractor's demonstrated performance with respect to the audit criteria provided.

35.0 SECTION 508 ACCESSIBILITY REQUIREMENTS FOR PRODUCTION SYSTEMS
35.1 ACCESSIBILITY REQUIREMENTS (SECTION 508): Section 508 of the Rehabilitation Act, as amended by the Workforce Investment Act of 1998 (P.L. 105-220) requires that when Federal agencies develop, procure, maintain, or use Electronic and Information Technology (EIT), they must ensure that it is accessible to people with disabilities. Federal employees and members of the public who have disabilities must have equal access to and use of information and data that is comparable to that enjoyed by non-disabled Federal employees and members of the public. All EIT deliverables within this work statement shall comply with the applicable technical and functional performance criteria of Section 508 unless exempt. Specifically, the following applicable EIT accessibility standards have been identified 35.2 SECTION 508 APPLICABLE EIT ACCESSIBILITY STANDARDS: Section 36 CFR 1194.21 Software Applications and Operating Systems, applies to all EIT software applications and operating systems procured or developed under this work statement including but not limited to GOTS and COTS software. In addition, this standard is to be applied to Web based applications when needed to fulfill the functional performance criteria. This standard also applies to some Web based applications as described within 36 CFR 1194.22. 36 CFR 1194.22 Web based Intranet and Internet Information and Applications, applies to all Web based deliverables, including documentation and reports procured or developed under this work statement. When any Web application uses a dynamic (non-static) interface, embeds custom user PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 67

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support control(s), embeds video or multimedia, uses proprietary or technical approaches such as, but not limited to, Flash or Asynchronous JavaScript and XML (AJAX) then 36 CFR 1194.24 Software standards also apply to fulfill functional performance criteria. 36 CFR 1194.24 Video and Multimedia Products, applies to all video and multimedia products that are procured or developed under this work statement. Any video or multimedia presentation shall also comply with the software standards (1194.21) when the presentation is through the use of a Web or Software application interface having user controls available. 36 CFR 1194.26 Desktop and Portable Computers, applies to all desktop and portable computers, including but not limited to laptops and personal data assistants (PDAs) that are procured or developed under this work statement. 36 CFR 1194.31 Functional Performance Criteria, applies to all EIT deliverables regardless of delivery method. All EIT deliverable shall use technical standards, regardless of technology, to fulfill the functional performance criteria. 36 CFR 1194.41 Information Documentation And Support, applies to all documents, reports, as well as help and support services. To ensure that documents and reports fulfill the required 1194.31 Functional Performance Criteria, they shall comply with the technical standard associated with Web based Intranet and Internet Information and Applications at a minimum. In addition, any help or support provided in this work statement that offer telephone support, such as, but not limited to, a help desk shall have the ability to transmit and receive messages using TTY.

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support 35.3 SECTION 508 APPLICABLE EXCEPTIONS: Exceptions for this work statement have been determined by DHS and only the exceptions described herein may be applied. DHS has identified the following exceptions that may apply: 36 CFR 1194.3(b) Incidental to Contract, all EIT that is exclusively owned and used by the Contractor to fulfill this work statement does not require compliance with Section 508. This exception does not apply to any EIT deliverable, service or item that will be used by any Federal employee(s) or member(s) of the public. This exception only applies to those Contractors assigned to fulfill the obligations of this work statement and for the purposes of this requirement, are not considered members of the public. 35.4 SECTION 508 COMPLIANCE REQUIREMENTS: (36 CFR 1194.2(b) pertaining to COTS or GOTS products) When procuring a product, each agency shall procure products which comply with the provisions in this part when such products are available in the commercial marketplace or when such products are developed in response to a Government solicitation. Agencies cannot claim a product as a whole is not commercially available because no product in the marketplace meets all the standards. If products are commercially available that may meet some but not all of the standards, the agency must procure the product that best meets the standards. When applying this standard, all procurements of EIT shall have documentation of market research that identify a list of products or services that first meet the agency business needs, and from that list of products or services, an analysis that the selected product met more of the accessibility requirements than the non-selected products as required by FAR 39.2. Any selection of a product or service that meets less accessibility standards due to a significant difficulty or expense shall only be permitted under an undue burden claim and requires authorization from the DHS Office of Accessible Systems and Technology (OAST) in accordance with DHS MD 4010.2.

36.0 SOFTWARE QUALITY ASSURANCE
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide qualified professionals to manage the requirements, documentation, changes, risks and testing of all mainframe and LAN applications. 36.1 REQUIRMENTS MANAGEMENT: The Contractor shall document, analyze and maintain all system software requirements via a Rational RequisitePro tool used to manage and trace all software requirements as part of the system lifecycle process. 36.2 CHANGE MANAGEMENT: The Contractor shall perform all change management functions necessary to comply with standard System Lifecycle Compliance processes. 36.3 OTHER DOCUMENTS: The Contractor shall maintain Functional Requirements Documents (FRD), a Requirements Traceability Matrix (RTM), Requirement Management Plan, a Configuration Management Plan, a Risk Management Plan, and a Software Quality Assurance Plan. These documents shall be reviewed at least annually to ensure accuracy and completeness. 37.0 SOR OPERATIONAL SUPPORT AND ONGOING MAINTENANCE
SYNOPSIS: The SOR requires operational support and ongoing maintenance for the period of the contract. In addition, the data gathered by the WYO companies and their support vendors on behalf of the NFIP is submitted to the Contractor in a well-defined format and according to a published schedule. 37.1 DOCUMENTATION: The Contractor shall completely create and maintain application, data and software documentation for all processes, systems and subsystems used in meeting the requirements of this SOW. Within two (2) business days of a request by the COR, the Contractor shall make this information available, with supporting detail, to FEMA. 37.2 SYSTEMS LOGIC: The Contractor shall document, maintain, and revise, as required, the logic for actuarial data maintenance, contracts in force, policies in force, earned premium, unearned premium, deferred acquisition costs and loss and loss adjustment reserves. Within two (2) business days of a request by the COR, the Contractor shall make this information available, with supporting detail, to FEMA. 37.3 DATA SUBMISSION: The Contractor shall support FEMA, the WYO Companies and the DSA contractor in the processing of received data, the resolution of data submission problems and the input of appropriate error corrections. The Contractor shall operate the system that edits and monitors the WYO data submissions at the quality level established for the TRRP Plan. The Contractor shall maintain and enhance systems and processes to provide improved data editing results and to facilitate the correction and resubmission of data, all of which is done in coordination with the COR. The Contractor shall report all data submission issues to the COR each month including all errors committed by WYO companies and their support vendors. 37.4 OPERATION OF TRRP PLAN: The Contractor shall support the operation of the TRRP Plan for the receipt of data from the WYO Companies and from the DSA contractor. The Contractor shall maintain systems and procedures for the submission and receipt of the data in a timely and accurate fashion. All TRRP Plan function testing results, such as the testing of various edit logic and jobs on the mainframe, shall be reported to the COR. 37.5 VALIDATION OF TRRP PLAN DATA: The TRRP Plan data shall be validated, edited, compared and balanced against the WYO Companies and the DSA contractor's reports of receipts, remittances to the Department of Treasury, draw downs, and disbursements. Additional validation of structure locations underwritten by the NFIP in respect to Digital Flood Insurance Rate Maps (D-FIRMS) and other geographic information systems is required to further ensure the accuracy of all TRRP data. 37.6 TRRP DOCUMENT MAINTENANCE: The Contractor shall maintain and enhance the TRRP Plan and the TRRP Edit Specification documents, in coordination with the COR. Within two (2) business days of a request by the COR, the Contractor shall make this information available, with supporting detail, to FEMA.

38.0 VERIFICATION AND VALIDATION
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall provide support to ensure systems and data accuracy through verification and validation efforts, periodic testing and reporting of the results of such. 38.1 EXPERT AND ANALYTICAL SYSTEMS SUPPORT: The Contractor shall provide commercially reasonable expert and analytical support to respond to the needs of FEMA to ensure systems and data accuracy. Verification is intended to check that TRRP and ancillary subsystems meet established and updated specifications. The Contractor shall perform tests to simulate proposed TRRP changes by performing a review and analysis of the modeled results. Following systems updates, the Contractor shall perform additional tests to validate continued proper function of the TRRP and ancillary subsystems. This support shall include, providing to FEMA periodic testing results demonstrating consistent and proper TRRP and other systems functions and complete test results following planned May and October rate and rule changes.

40.0 TRANSITION OF SERVICES
SYNOPSIS: The Contractor shall, upon notice from the CO or COR, prepare a transition plan to facilitate a smooth and orderly transition of FEMA property to FEMA or another contractor. This smooth and orderly transition includes the requirement that there can be no disruption of any NFIP production service identified and described within this SOW. To facilitate a smooth and orderly transition, the Contractor shall accept data generated by FEMA, the incumbent or other governmental systems that have been transferred to FEMA or another contractor as may be required to maintain operations throughout the transition. 40.1 TRANSITION PLAN: The transition plan shall include all actions necessary to successfully complete the transfer of operational responsibility for the SOR. The Contractor shall deliver a copy of the SOR and copies of all applicable input data files and processing outputs for a selected processing cycle. 40.2 TRANSITION-IN AND TRANSITION-OUT SERVICES: The Contractor shall execute a six (6) month transition period during which the Contractor shall overlap with the current contractor. Upon execution of contract, Contractor will contact the COR to schedule the Transition-In Plan briefing, create and submit the Transition-In Plan, and contact the current contractor to advise them of the appropriate points of contact to coordinate performance of shared work. During the Transition-In period, the Contractor shall become familiar with the performance requirements and establish the management organization. The transition period provides time for the Contractor to prepare for a seamless transition of services. The Contractor shall schedule and attend a weekly transition meeting during the Transition-In period. The attendees shall include the FEMA Contracting Officer Representative (COR), the incumbent Bureau and Statistical Agent (BSA) contractor, the incumbent Legacy Systems Services (LSS) contractor and any additional parties that FEMA designates. The meeting shall address progress, planned work and any problems with the potential solution. The Transition-In Deliverables are listed in the Deliverables Chart. At any time and consistent with the executed contract, if the Contractor is replaced by another contractor, a formal Transition-Out plan shall be developed, the approach of which shall address the PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 73

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support circumstances of the transition. The Contractor shall maintain staff to provide service continuity and transition support until the transition is complete. All developed materials and data are property of FEMA. The Contractor shall transition operation of the SOR to FEMA at the request of the CO. The CO will communicate the transition request to allow the necessary time allowable for a successful transfer. The CO will also initiate Service Level Agreements (SLAs) for the transition. The Contractor shall return all sensitive DHS information and IT resources provided during the life of this contract. The Contractor shall certify that all DHS information has been purged from any contractor owned system used to store or process DHS information. Electronic media must be sanitized in accordance with applicable guidance and procedure contained in DHS 4300A.

SOR

SYNOPSIS: The Government owns all of the Application Computer Code (Applications) that is used to administer the NFIP (mainframe, distributed and workstation), the equipment necessary to support the distributed processing identified herein (Distributed GFE), the operating systems and related supporting software (security, reporting, DBMS, tools utilities, etc.) (Software) for the distributed environment, and all the current and historical program data related to the NFIP (Data). The Government does not own the mainframe hardware or its related Software. The Contractor shall be responsible for maintaining and operating the entire existing NFIP computing environment, defined as Applications, Software, mainframe hardware, distributed hardware, and Data. Section 43 contains an overview of the computing resources that are used to support the NFIP. The SOR is comprised of a mainframe environment that processes approximately two (2) million lines of JCL, FOCUS, COBOL and utility code distributed among 6,200 modules. The aggregate Data managed in this environment is approximately 31 TB of which 6 TB is DASD storage and 25 TB is offline tape storage. The distributed environment consists of 71 servers and 23 network devices (routers, switches firewalls and storage) that utilize 35 TB of server and network storage. 41.1 DISTRIBUTED PRODUCTION ENVIRONMENT: FEMA owns the entire distributed server and network equipment inventory identified in table Computing Resources 43-1. The tables Computing Resources 43-6 and Computing Resources 43-9 identify the related software. The Contractor shall either relocate or propose an alternative solution to relocating all Distributed Production GFE from its current locations in Landover, MD and Norwich, CT to the Contractor's designated facility. Relocation includes uninstalling, packing, transporting, and reinstalling the Distributed GFE at the Contractor's designated facility. Any facility must meet all applicable physical and logical security guidance in DHS 4300A.

PLACE OF PERFORMANCE
SYNOPSIS: The government requires that the Contractor facilitate the government's access to both the personnel and physical locations for the purpose of meeting attendance, problem resolution and contract monitoring while benefitting from the Contractor's ability to utilize the most cost effective geographical locations. The government requires support throughout the normal business day5 and potentially around the clock during flood events. Travel and related expenses that the Contractor would need to incur to provide the functions described herein shall be included in the response. The Contractor shall provide one (1) fully functional video conference facility at each location. PROXIMITY TO THE NATIONAL CAPITAL REGION: The Contractor shall situate one (1) subject matter expert within the NCR for each Section 1-40 requirements. Additionally, appropriate management shall be situated in the NCR. These requirements facilitate face to face access to the array of subject matter experts and management that the government feels is crucial to the ongoing support needs of the NFIP. The government anticipates that periodic access will also be required to staff that may not be located in the NCR. These needs would be met via teleconference or video conference.6 The NCR requirement does not apply to the personnel not listed in the above section, "Proximity to the National Capital Region." The location for this staff is left to the Contractor to decide for itself. The NCR requirement does not apply to the location of the production mainframe and distributed environments. The location of the development and test facilities for both mainframe and distributed environments is left to the Contractor to decide for itself.

Functions 42-6 Financial Operations
Active audit interaction -- The Contractor shall be actively engaged in all audits, regulatory reviews, risk assessments and data requests while representing the primary depository of financial and statistical data. The Contractor shall have an active role and is the primary point of contact in leading the effect by directing coordination with all WYO companies and the DSA contractor and ensure that internal controls are in-place consistent with the guidance. Actuarial ad-hoc analysis of experience, pricing and product development -- The Contractor's actuary acting as the SME's is responsible for responding to ad-hoc requests for data and other support. Actuarial cash flow and Retro Analysis reporting -- The Contractor's Actuary team is responsible for the monthly development and distribution of the cash flow analysis of expected demand and the retro analysis of actual loss experience compared to the original loss reserve estimate. Ad-Hoc financial analysis, assessments and report -- The Contractor shall respond to all requests for ad-hoc reports and analysis of NFIP program data in support of annual or nonrecurring assessments by FEMA staff, Mitigation, regulatory groups, and other stakeholders. Annual Statement of Actuarial Opinion -- The Contractor's Actuary is responsible for delivery of the Annual Statement of Actuarial Opinion that provides the degree of assurance that the annual estimated loss reserves are reasonable within the expected range. This report supports the basis for assessing the NFIP programs obligations and financial viability. Assist in the resolution of data submission and correction problems: Upon identification of submission errors the Contractor is responsible for leading and coordinating the correction with the respective WYO company and for validation of the resubmitted data prior to furthering the preparation of the consolidated financial statements. Attend Audit Meetings and Walkthroughs CFO Insurance Services Statements - The Contractor shall support the FEMA/CFO's office financial reporting requirements related to the NFIP program. The Contractor shall be the primary point of contact in leading the effort by preparation of consolidated financial statements, performance data, quarterly and annual forecasts, loss reserve development, cash flow analysis, and including drafting notes to the FEMA/CFO's external financial statements. The Contractor also represents insurance financial SME's is support of drafting related SOP's.

Processing - Detailed report of cash deposits -- The Contractor shall provide monthly reporting of cash receipts and deposits made by the Program. The Contractor must report its cash deposit activity. Processing - Report of reconciliation discrepancies -- The Contractor shall provide a monthly report disclosing the reporting status of WYO companies and the DSA contractor that had reporting errors in their initial monthly financial and statistical submissions and the identification and status of the required correction to allow inclusion in the period consolidated financial statements.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 82

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support Processing -- The Contractor shall provide a report of financial and statistical variances - The variance report is an extensive development effort that is a primary NFIP Program tool to assess WYO Company and DSA contractor compliance with defined standards of reporting or predetermined tolerance levels. Target areas include finance and statistical variance presentation of written premium, losses paid, and federal policy fee. Production is followed by contacting WYO companies to resolve, request corrective action plans, and to coordinate adjustments. The variance report is a source tool for reporting compliance to the Standards Committee. Processing -- The Contractor shall provide a report of Letter of Credit activity. Consolidated monthly and annual report of deposits (letter of credit) for all WYO companies and the DSA contractor, including the related expenses incurred. All Contractors are responsible for reporting their Letter of Credit activity. Processing -- The Contractor shall provide a Report of outstanding accounts receivable. The monthly receivable report discloses all outstanding claim overpayments and other receivables identified by claim reinspection and other review practices. Processing -- The Contractor shall provide a report of prior term refunds. The monthly prior term refund presents refunds for policy terms greater than two (2) years prior. Requests shall be validated by the underwriting group, quantified and forwarded to the finance group for disbursement of the refund. Processing -- The Contractor shall provide a report of special travel allowances. The monthly report of special travel allowance reflects disbursements to claim adjusters for extended periods at disaster sites based on payable amounts disclosed in the NFIP financial policy. Processing/Data Integrity -- The Contractor shall provide Letter. Letters of Credit and Disbursements, Receipt, approval and disbursement of LOC funds for all expenses related to Disaster Responses, Reinspections, and postage in additional to all other COR approved expenses. Relate financial data to statistical data -- The Contractor shall perform analytics and reviews upon receipt of WYO and DSA contractor monthly financial and statistical data to ensure that the underlying policy and claims records reconcile with the same period reported financial submissions. Research and Prepare NFR Responses Risk and Compliance -- The Contractor shall provide risk and compliance activities. This process includes the active and ongoing sustainment of internal control, the safeguard as program assets and development of relevant financial procedures to ensure adherence with rules, policies, GAAP, and regulatory oversight. Support annual rate reviews and rate and rule revisions -- The Contractor's Actuary is responsible for analysis and support of FEMA's actuarial staff related to rate-reviews and assessment of the resulting rate and rule revisions. Support Mitigation and risk assessment aspects -- The Contractor shall respond to ongoing requests to provide documents and proof of compliance and controls in response to FEMA Mitigation requests and related risk assessments. PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 83

Statement of Work National Flood Insurance Program IT Systems and Support WYO Standards Committee -- The Contractor shall provide support information to FEMA and The WYO Standards Committee - The Contractor shall respond to ongoing requests to perform analysis in support of FEMA oversight groups, for rate-reviews and other assessments. This information supports performance analysis requested by FEMA staff, Mitigation, data for the Standards Committee corrective actions or the IBHS meeting requirements.

43.0 SOR COMPUTING RESOURCES AND ENVIRONMENT
SYNOPSIS: The SOR computing environment consists of mainframe, distributed and workstation hardware and software. The tables in this section identify the hardware (where applicable) and the software that support the NFIP in the categories shown below.

Software

Table 32 Hardware and Software Cross Reference

The NFIP owns the Distributed hardware that supports the distributed and web based applications. The NFIP does not own the mainframe hardware that runs its legacy systems, choosing instead to purchase the MIPS it needs as appropriate. The Contractor shall plan a migration of all Government-owned hardware and software to a FEMA approved datacenter. The response to the proposal must include a high level draft plan that demonstrates the Contractor's ability to successfully execute this migration. A detailed migration plan shall have a target completion date within forty five (45) days of the award date and which provides a 15 day period for review by FEMA. Neither migration plan is part of the Transition-In plan but the detailed migration plan is expected to be referenced in the Transition-In plan. The detailed migration plan must be successfully executed within seven (7) months of its acceptance by FEMA. The NFIP IT legacy system services to be provided for the mainframe and distributed environments shall minimally include those listed in Computing Resources 43-3 on page 93. The Contractor shall execute the plan upon acceptance of said plan by FEMA.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 109

QUALITY ASSURANCE SURVEILLANCE PLAN NATIONAL FLOOD INSURANCE PROGRAM INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY SYSTEMS AND SUPPORT (NFIP ITS&S)
To provide systems and support services to the National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP) and its stakeholders. The contractor will be required to adhere to the guidelines described herein.

PURPOSE
This Government's Quality Assurance Surveillance Plan (QASP) has been developed to evaluate contractor actions while implementing the Statement of Work (SOW) for the National Flood Insurance Program Information Technology Systems and Support contract (NFIP ITS&S). It is designed to provide an effective surveillance method of monitoring contractor performance for each listed requirement of the SOW. The QASP explains: what will be monitored, how monitoring will take place, who will conduct the monitoring, and how monitoring efforts and results will be documented. This QASP is based on the premise that the Government desires to maintain a quality standard in operating, maintaining, and providing the service with the best means of achieving this objective. The contractor is responsible for management and quality control actions to meet the terms of the contract. The role of the Government in quality assurance is to ensure contract standards are achieved and to provide an effective surveillance method to monitor the contractor's performance relative to the requirements listed in the agreement. The QASP illustrates the systematic method the Government (or its designated representative) will use to evaluate the services the contractor is required to furnish. The contractor is required to develop a comprehensive program of inspections and monitoring actions and to document its approach in a Quality Control Plan (QCP). The contractor's QCP, upon approval by the Government, will be made a part of the resulting contractual agreement. The first major step to ensuring a "self-correcting" contract is to ensure that the QCP provides the measures needed to lead the contractor to success. Once the QCP is approved, careful application of the process and standards presented in the remainder of this document will ensure a robust quality assurance program. This QASP is a "living document" and the Government may review and revise it on a regular basis. However, the Government shall coordinate changes with the contractor. Updates shall ensure that the QASP remains a valid, useful, and enforceable document. Copies of the original QASP and revisions shall be provided to the contractor and Government officials implementing surveillance activities.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104

1

QUALITY ASSURANCE SURVEILLANCE PLAN GOVERNMENT ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES
The following personnel shall oversee and coordinate surveillance activities: a. Contracting Officer (CO) - The CO shall ensure performance of all necessary actions for effective contracting, ensure compliance with the contract terms, and shall safeguard the interests of the United States in the contractual relationship. The CO shall also assure that the contractor receives impartial, fair, and equitable treatment under this contract. The CO is ultimately responsible for the final determination of the adequacy of the contractor's performance. Assigned CO: Carolyn Ward Organization or Agency: Federal Emergency Management Agency Telephone: 202.646.4654 Email: Carolyn. Ward@fema.dhs.gov
b. Contracting Officer's Representative (COR) - The COR is responsible for technical

administration of the contract and shall assure proper Government surveillance of the contractor's performance. The COR shall keep a quality assurance file. At the conclusion of the contract or when requested by the CO, the contractor shall provide documentation to the CO that details the surveillance conducted and the results. The COR is not empowered to make any contractual commitments or to authorize any contractual changes on the Government's behalf. The contractor shall refer any changes they deem may affect contract price, terms, or conditions to the CO for action. Assigned COR: TBD Telephone: Email:

QUALITY CONTROL PLAN

As a part of its agreement with the Government, the contractor is required to develop, implement, and maintain a Quality Control Plan (QCP) that illustrates the methods it will use to review its performance to ensure it conforms to the performance requirements. See Attachment 1: Performance Requirements Summary for performance objectives which will be reviewed by the Government. The contractor should also perform such reviews in order to validate its operations and assure the Government that the services meet the performance standards. The contractor's QCP should include monitoring methods that ensure and demonstrate its compliance with the performance standards. This includes inspection methods and schedules that are consistent with the regular reviews conducted by the government. The reports and other results generated by the contractor's QCP activities should be provided to the COR as requested. The frequency and type of the contractor's reviews should be consistent with what is necessary in order to ensure compliance with the performance standards, but no less frequent than what PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 2

QUALITY ASSURANCE SURVEILLANCE PLAN
is described in the Statement of Work and the Government's Performance Monitoring Tool (See Attachment 2). The contractor is encouraged not to limit its inspection to only the processes outlined in the Government's standard; however, certain key documents must be provided by the contractor to assure the Government that the services meet the performance standards. Listed below is a partial list of the documentation that must be generated and made available to the COR for inspection. The list is intended as illustrative and is not all-inclusive. The contractor must develop and implement a program that addresses the specific requirement of each standard and the means it will use to document compliance. ˇ Written policies and procedures to implement and assess operational requirements of the standard ˇ Documentation and recording keeping that ensure ongoing operational compliance with the standards (e.g.; inventories, logbooks, register of receipts, reports, etc.) ˇ Staff training records ˇ Investigative reports ˇ Medical records ˇ Records of investigative actions taken ˇ Equipment inspections ˇ System tests and evaluation

METHOD OF SURVEILLANCE
The Contracting Officer Representative (COR) or their designee will survey the appropriate work of the contractor and observe the contractor performing the tasks or review documentation, as appropriate. The COR or his or her designee will conduct evaluations of all of items identified in the below Performance Requirements Summary (PRS) in a manner consistent with the Quality Assurance Surveillance Plan, or any other method at the COR's discretion. The COR may receive input through customer feedback as well as NFIP personnel and other Government personnel. Contractor performance will be surveyed to determine if it meets the contract standards. A variety of surveillance methods may be used. Random Sampling FEMA may conduct random sampling when the COR or designated FEMA representatives samples services to determine if the level of performance is acceptable based on a statistically random sample. Periodic Inspection of the Processes or Output FEMA shall conduct monthly reviews either of reports or at the contractor's site; FEMA may conduct periodic inspections when the COR or designated FEMA representative chooses the location and time to conduct surveillance in other than a statistically random manner.

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104

3

QUALITY ASSURANCE SURVEILLANCE PLAN
Stakeholder Feedback FEMA may use validated stakeholder feedback as the basis for actions against the contractor; other FEMA employees and WYO companies are considered stakeholders to this contract.

PERFORMANCE EVALUATION
Performance of a service will be evaluated to determine whether or not it meets the performance requirements of the contract. When the performance requirement is not met, the Contracting Officer will issue a Discrepancy Report (DR) to the contractor. The Discrepancy Report is drafted by the COR, who forwards it to the Contracting Officer. The contractor shall respond to the Discrepancy Report by completing the appropriate blocks of the form and returning it to the Contracting Officer within 15 calendar days of receipt. Upon evaluation of the contractor's response to a Discrepancy Response the contractor's payment for the month in which the performance in question occurred will be calculated as stated in the contractor payment section. In the case of Discrepancy Reports issued as the result of other methods of surveillance, the Contracting Officer shall take appropriate measures according to the clause entitled "Inspection of Services."

RATINGS
Metrics and methods are designed to determine if performance exceeds, meets, or does not meet a given standard and acceptable quality level. A rating scale shall be used to determine a positive, neutral, or negative outcome. The following ratings shall be used:
EXCEEDED: MET: UNMET:

Performance significantly exceeds contract requirements to the Government's benefit. Performance meets contractual requirements. Performance does not meet contractual requirements.

QUALITY ASSURANCE SURVEILLANCE PLAN Attachment 1: PERFORMANCE REQUIREMENTS SUMMARY (PRS)
Performance Objective: Lists the performance objectives that the Government will survey. The absence of any contract requirement from the QASP shall not detract from its enforceability to limit the rights or remedies of the Government under any other provisions of the contract, including the clauses entitled "Inspection of Services" and "Default." Required Service: Defines the standard of performance for each listed objective. Performance Standard: Sets forth the minimum allowable deviation from the standard performance which may occur before the Government will invoke the payment computation formula for an incentive; and/or sets forth the maximum deviation from the standard performance before the Government will invoke the payment computation formula for the disincentive. The column has alpha-bullets which correspond to bullets of the same in Column 5 (Performance Incentive/Disincentive). Method of Surveillance: Sets forth the surveillance methods the Government will use to evaluate the contractor's performance for the listed tasks. This column also establishes the period of planned surveillance. Performance Incentive/Disincentive: Sets forth the performance evaluation area percentage weighting that the listed contract requirements represents.

____________________________________________________________________________________ ALL OCCUPATIONS LISTED ABOVE RECEIVE THE FOLLOWING BENEFITS: HEALTH & WELFARE: $4.02 per hour or $160.80 per week or $696.79 per month VACATION: 2 weeks paid vacation after 1 year of service with a contractor or successor; 3 weeks after 5 years, and 4 weeks after 15 years. Length of service includes the whole span of continuous service with the present contractor or successor, wherever employed, and with the predecessor contractors in the performance of similar work at the same Federal facility. (Reg. 29 CFR 4.173) HOLIDAYS: A minimum of ten paid holidays per year, New Year's Day, Martin Luther King Jr's Birthday, Washington's Birthday, Memorial Day, Independence Day, Labor Day, Columbus Day, Veterans' Day, Thanksgiving Day, and Christmas Day. (A contractor may substitute for any of the named holidays another day off with pay in accordance with a plan communicated to the employees involved.) (See 29 CFR 4174)

THE OCCUPATIONS WHICH HAVE NUMBERED FOOTNOTES IN PARENTHESES RECEIVE THE FOLLOWING: 1) COMPUTER EMPLOYEES: Under the SCA at section 8(b), this wage determination does not apply to any employee who individually qualifies as a bona fide executive, administrative, or professional employee as defined in 29 C.F.R. Part 541. Because most Computer System Analysts and Computer Programmers who are compensated at a rate not less than $27.63 (or on a salary or fee basis at a rate not less than $455 per week) an hour would likely qualify as exempt computer professionals, (29 C.F.R. 541. 400) wage rates may not be listed on this wage determination for all occupations within those job families. In addition, because this wage determination may not list a wage rate for some or all occupations within those job families if the survey data indicates that the prevailing wage rate for the occupation equals or exceeds $27.63 per hour conformances may be necessary for certain nonexempt employees. For example, if an individual employee is nonexempt but nevertheless performs duties within the scope of one of the Computer Systems Analyst or Computer Programmer

http://www.wdol.gov/wdol/scafiles/std/05-2103.txt?v=14

10/31/2014

Page 8 of 10

occupations for which this wage determination does not specify an SCA wage rate, then the wage rate for that employee must be conformed in accordance with the conformance procedures described in the conformance note included on this wage determination. Additionally, because job titles vary widely and change quickly in the computer industry, job titles are not determinative of the application of the computer professional exemption. Therefore, the exemption applies only to computer employees who satisfy the compensation requirements and whose primary duty consists of: (1) The application of systems analysis techniques and procedures, including consulting with users, to determine hardware, software or system functional specifications; (2) The design, development, documentation, analysis, creation, testing or modification of computer systems or programs, including prototypes, based on and related to user or system design specifications; (3) The design, documentation, testing, creation or modification of computer programs related to machine operating systems; or (4) A combination of the aforementioned duties, the performance of which requires the same level of skills. (29 C.F.R. 541.400). 2) AIR TRAFFIC CONTROLLERS AND WEATHER OBSERVERS - NIGHT PAY & SUNDAY PAY: If you work at night as part of a regular tour of duty, you will earn a night differential and receive an additional 10% of basic pay for any hours worked between 6pm and 6am. If you are a full-time employed (40 hours a week) and Sunday is part of your regularly scheduled workweek, you are paid at your rate of basic pay plus a Sunday premium of 25% of your basic rate for each hour of Sunday work which is not overtime (i.e. occasional work on Sunday outside the normal tour of duty is considered overtime work).

HAZARDOUS PAY DIFFERENTIAL: An 8 percent differential is applicable to employees employed in a position that represents a high degree of hazard when working with or in close proximity to ordinance, explosives, and incendiary materials. This includes work such as screening, blending, dying, mixing, and pressing of sensitive ordance, explosives, and pyrotechnic compositions such as lead azide, black powder and photoflash powder. All dry-house activities involving propellants or explosives. Demilitarization, modification, renovation, demolition, and maintenance operations on sensitive ordnance, explosives and incendiary materials. All operations involving regrading and cleaning of artillery ranges. A 4 percent differential is applicable to employees employed in a position that represents a low degree of hazard when working with, or in close proximity to ordance, (or employees possibly adjacent to) explosives and incendiary materials which involves potential injury such as laceration of hands, face, or arms of the employee engaged in the operation, irritation of the skin, minor burns and the like; minimal damage to immediate or adjacent work area or equipment being used. All operations involving, unloading, storage, and hauling of ordance, explosive, and incendiary ordnance material other than small arms ammunition. These differentials are only applicable to work that has been specifically designated by the agency for ordance, explosives, and incendiary material differential pay. ** UNIFORM ALLOWANCE ** If employees are required to wear uniforms in the performance of this contract (either by the terms of the Government contract, by the employer, by the state or local law, etc.), the cost of furnishing such uniforms and maintaining (by laundering or dry cleaning) such uniforms is an expense that may not be borne by an employee where such cost reduces the hourly rate below that required by the wage determination. The Department of Labor will accept payment in accordance with the following standards as compliance:

http://www.wdol.gov/wdol/scafiles/std/05-2103.txt?v=14

10/31/2014

Page 9 of 10

The contractor or subcontractor is required to furnish all employees with an adequate number of uniforms without cost or to reimburse employees for the actual cost of the uniforms. In addition, where uniform cleaning and maintenance is made the responsibility of the employee, all contractors and subcontractors subject to this wage determination shall (in the absence of a bona fide collective bargaining agreement providing for a different amount, or the furnishing of contrary affirmative proof as to the actual cost), reimburse all employees for such cleaning and maintenance at a rate of $3.35 per week (or $.67 cents per day). However, in those instances where the uniforms furnished are made of "wash and wear" materials, may be routinely washed and dried with other personal garments, and do not require any special treatment such as dry cleaning, daily washing, or commercial laundering in order to meet the cleanliness or appearance standards set by the terms of the Government contract, by the contractor, by law, or by the nature of the work, there is no requirement that employees be reimbursed for uniform maintenance costs. The duties of employees under job titles listed are those described in the "Service Contract Act Directory of Occupations", Fifth Edition, April 2006, unless otherwise indicated. Copies of the Directory are available on the Internet. A links to the Directory may be found on the WHD home page at http://www.dol. gov/esa/whd/ or through the Wage Determinations On-Line (WDOL) Web site at http://wdol.gov/. REQUEST FOR AUTHORIZATION OF ADDITIONAL CLASSIFICATION AND WAGE RATE {Standard Form 1444 (SF 1444)} Conformance Process: The contracting officer shall require that any class of service employee which is not listed herein and which is to be employed under the contract (i.e., the work to be performed is not performed by any classification listed in the wage determination), be classified by the contractor so as to provide a reasonable relationship (i.e., appropriate level of skill comparison) between such unlisted classifications and the classifications listed in the wage determination. Such conformed classes of employees shall be paid the monetary wages and furnished the fringe benefits as are determined. Such conforming process shall be initiated by the contractor prior to the performance of contract work by such unlisted class(es) of employees. The conformed classification, wage rate, and/or fringe benefits shall be retroactive to the commencement date of the contract. {See Section 4.6 (C)(vi)} When multiple wage determinations are included in a contract, a separate SF 1444 should be prepared for each wage determination to which a class(es) is to be conformed. The process for preparing a conformance request is as follows: 1) When preparing the bid, the contractor identifies the need for a conformed occupation(s) and computes a proposed rate(s). 2) After contract award, the contractor prepares a written report listing in order proposed classification title(s), a Federal grade equivalency (FGE) for each proposed classification(s), job description(s), and rationale for proposed wage rate(s), including information regarding the agreement or disagreement of the authorized representative of the employees involved, or where there is no authorized representative, the employees themselves. This report should be submitted to the contracting officer no later than 30 days after such unlisted class(es) of employees performs any contract work. 3) The contracting officer reviews the proposed action and promptly submits a report of the action, together with the agency's recommendations and pertinent information including the position of the contractor and the employees, to the Wage and Hour Division, Employment Standards Administration, U.S. Department of Labor, for review. (See section 4.6(b)(2) of Regulations 29 CFR Part 4).

http://www.wdol.gov/wdol/scafiles/std/05-2103.txt?v=14

10/31/2014

Page 10 of 10

4) Within 30 days of receipt, the Wage and Hour Division approves, modifies, or disapproves the action via transmittal to the agency contracting officer, or notifies the contracting officer that additional time will be required to process the request. 5) The contracting officer transmits the Wage and Hour decision to the contractor. 6) The contractor informs the affected employees. Information required by the Regulations must be submitted on SF 1444 or bond paper. When preparing a conformance request, the "Service Contract Act Directory of Occupations" (the Directory) should be used to compare job definitions to insure that duties requested are not performed by a classification already listed in the wage determination. Remember, it is not the job title, but the required tasks that determine whether a class is included in an established wage determination. Conformances may not be used to artificially split, combine, or subdivide classifications listed in the wage determination.

Task 5.0 Pricing Scenario The National Hurricane Center (NHC) is tracking a storm that exited the northwestern coast of Africa on August 8, 2014, and the circulation center is well defined. The storm is anticipated to strengthen to hurricane force and projected to impact the east coast if it remains on its current track. On August 15, 2014, NHC announced the storm strengthened to Category III, with sustained winds of 125 mph, (intensity on the Saffir­Simpson scale) and classified a major hurricane. If the storm remains on its current path; the storm will lash the east coast with high waves, major coastal flooding, severe damage to infrastructure, residential and commercial buildings and communications will be impacted. Businesses and residents are warned to prepare for the onslaught of this major storm and evacuations are mandatory along the east coast. Within the past 24-hours the NHC announced the hurricane will remain on its projected track with extreme intensification to a Category IV, and sustained winds of 152 mph making landfall at Hialeah, Florida with winds extending as far inland as Hernando County. The current path of the storm will track up the east coast from Florida to Maine. This storm is dangerous and evacuations are mandatory, the storm will intensify and lose strength as it tracks up the coast, but will cause major wind and flood damage to buildings and infrastructure ˇ FEMA is in a state of readiness and have activated the NRCC and FEMA Regional Offices, etc. FEMA works in conjunction with their contractors who are required to respond and report to FEMA, how will this be accomplished with a storm of this magnitude affecting eleven states.

GOVERNMENT QUALITY ASSURANCE SURVEILLANCE The government will perform quality assurance procedures that will be necessary to verify that performance is in accordance with the terms of the contract. Government quality assurance will be perform routinely by the COR; however, other activities may be called upon to support this effort as required. For those task listed in the Statement of Work (SOW); the Project Officer or designated quality assurance evaluators will record all surveillance observations and will maintain a file of all inspection results. Government surveillance of tasks not listed in the SOW may occur during the performance of the contract. Such surveillance will be done according to standard inspection procedures or other contract provision. Successive months of unsatisfactory performance may result in other appropriate action(s) by the contracting officer in accordance with the Inspection of Service clause, Performance Based Payments clause, including Termination for Default. Any action taken by the contracting officer as a result of surveillance will be in accordance with the terms of this contract. PERFORMANCE SURVEILLANCE The government may use a variety of surveillance methods to evaluate the contractor's performance. These include, but are not limited to, random sampling of recurring services, periodic surveillance or the contractor's quality control program, the annual Certified Public Accountant (CPA) audit of the financial statements and customer complaints.

A payment request means any invoice or request for contract financing payment requesting reimbursement for supplies or services rendered. The Contractor shall not be paid more frequently than on a monthly basis. Contractors must submit vouchers electronically in pdf format to the FEMA Finance Center at FEMA- Finance-Vendor-Payments@fema.dhs.gov. The submission of vouchers electronically will reduce correspondence and other causes for delay to a minimum and will facilitate prompt payment to the Contractor. Paper vouchers mailed to the finance center will not be processed for payment. If the Contractor is unable to submit a payment request in electronic form, the contractor shall submit the payment request using a method mutually agreed to by the Contractor, the Contracting Officer, and the payment office. G.4 Invoice Instructions: Items 0002-0006, 2002-2004, 3002-3004, 4002-4004: INVOICE PREPARATION INSTRUCTIONS SF 1035 The SF 1035 will be used for additional information required by the Contracting Officer and should be submitted as a continuation sheet to the SF 1034. Suitable self-designed forms may be submitted instead of the SF 1035 as long as they contain the information required. The information required on the SF 1035 may differ in format and content depending on the type of cost reimbursable contract (cost plus fixed fee, cost plus incentive fee, time and materials, etc.) Amounts claimed on vouchers must be based on records maintained by the contractor to show by major cost element the amounts claimed for reimbursement for each applicable contract. The records must be maintained based on the contractor's fiscal year and should include reconciliations of any differences between the costs incurred per books and amounts claimed for reimbursement. The information which a contractor is required to submit in its Standard Form 1035 is set forth as follows: a. Show, as applicable, the target or estimated costs, target or fixed-fee, and total contract value, as adjusted by any modifications to the contract or order. The FAR permits the contracting officer to withhold a percentage of fixed fee until a reserve is set aside in an amount that is considered necessary to protect the Government's interest. b. Each invoice or voucher for reimbursement shall include sufficient detail to identify costs properly chargeable to the contract. In addition, each invoice or voucher for reimbursement of costs shall detail the total vouchered charges by showing current and cumulative costs by cost element as follows: (1) Direct Labor. For cost type contracts, list each total labor costs by indirect allocation base separately. For T&M contracts, list each labor category, rate per labor hour, hours worked, and extended total labor dollars per labor category. (2) Premium Pay/Overtime. List each labor category, rate per labor hour, hours worked, and the extended total labor dollars per labor category. Note: Advance written authorization must be received from the contracting officer to work overtime or to pay premium rates; therefore, identify the contracting officer's written authorization to the contractor. (3) Fringe Benefits. If fringe benefits are included in the overhead pool, no entry is required. If the contract allows for a separate fringe benefit pool, cite the rate, base, and
PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 10

extended amount. (4) Materials, Supplies, Equipment. Show those items normally treated as direct costs. Expendable items need not be itemized and may be grouped into major classifications such as office supplies. However, items valued at $5,000 or more must be itemized. See (FAR) 48 CFR part 45, Government Property, for reporting of property. (5) Travel. List the name and title of traveler, place of travel, and travel dates. Show the amount for the mode of travel (i.e., airline, private auto, taxi, etc.), lodging, meals, and other incidental expenses separately, on a daily basis. Travel costs for consultants must be shown separately and also supported. (6) Other Direct Costs. Itemize those costs that cannot be placed in categories (1) through (5)above. Categorize these costs to the extent possible. (7) Total Direct Costs. Cite the sum of categories (1) through (6) above. (8) Overhead. Cite the rate, base, and extended amount. (9) G&A Expense. Cite the rate, base, and extended amount. (10) Total Costs. Cite the sum of categories (7) through (9) above. (11) Fee. Cite the rate, base, and extended amount. (12) Total Cost and Fee Claimed. Enter this amount on the SF 1034. c. Payments of invoices or vouchers submitted under this contract shall be made in accordance with FAR clause 52.232-20 "Limitation of Cost" (APR 1984) for Cost contracts. The invoice must be in accordance with FAR 32.905. Contractors shall not submit invoices more frequently than once every 30 days. Invoices submitted more frequently shall be rejected for not being in compliance with the terms and conditions of this contract. e. Invoices or vouchers, and any required supporting documentation, must be properly identifiable with the Name of contractor, date of the invoice/voucher, contract number, contract line item, name and address or EFT information that payment is to be sent to, and the name, title and phone number of the point of contact at the contractor's facility in case of a defective invoice/voucher. d. Invoice or vouchers for payment of costs, if any shall include the total cumulative cost, if any previously invoiced. Each cost invoice or voucher for reimbursement shall include sufficient detail to identify costs properly chargeable to the contract. In addition, each invoice or voucher for reimbursement of costs shall detail the total voucher charges by showing current and cumulative costs in the following manner:

PERFORMANCE BASED PAYMENTS Invoices will be accepted and approved in accordance with 52.232-32 and the procedures outlined below. Each month the COR will evaluate the contractor in accordance with the Quality Assurance Surveillance Plan (QASP) located in Section J, Attachment III and the Deliverables Acceptance Sheet, Attachment IV. If all of the deliverables, listed in Section F, for the 30 day period have not been received, accepted, and approved by the COR the monthly payment will be rejected. Late submissions of the required deliverables will be documented as outlined in the QASP and made a part of the contract file to be used for past performance history. No payment will be approved until ALL of the required deliverables have been submitted to the COR for review, acceptance, and approval.

USE OF HARDWARE AND/OR SOFTWARE MONITORS Contractors shall permit inclusion or attachment of such devices as the government may choose to employ for purposes of examining or measuring the activities within the computer system. Devices such as hardware monitors, which may require physical connection to the computer system, and devices such as software monitors, which may require portions of the computer system's control software to be displaced, are specifically included in this the category. The contractor may not prohibit installation of such devices unless the particular device will cause significant or permanent damage to the computer system. The contractor shall assist the government in identifying and locating device connections when requested by the government if the contractor provides such service to other customers. Cost for this service, if any, is stated in section B of this contract. SITE PREPARATION The government shall prepare the site at its own expense and in accordance with the equipment environmental specifications furnished by the contractor in the proposal. Any alterations or modifications in site preparation which are directly attributed to incomplete or erroneous equipment environmental specifications provided by the contractor which would involve additional expenses to the government shall be made at the expense of the contractor.

RISK OF LOSS OR DAMAGE LEASE In the case of leased equipment, the government is relieved of all risks of loss or damage to the equipment during periods of transportation and installation, and during the entire time the equipment is in the possession of the government, except for:
PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 14

(i) loss or damage caused by nuclear reaction, nuclear radiation, radioactive contamination, war, insurrection, civil strife, rebellion, weapons of war; or (ii) negligence on the part of the government or its agents, provided, however, that the government shall be relieved of the liability for such risks or damage due to negligence if any commercial customer for the contractor is relieved of such liability under like circumstances.

WAIVER OF DELIVERY SCHEDULE None of the following shall be regarded as an extension, waiver, or abandonment of the delivery schedule or a waiver of the government's right to terminate for default: (i) Delay by the government in terminating for default; (ii) Acceptance of delinquent deliveries; and (iii) Acceptance or approval of samples submitted either after default in delivery or in sufficient time for the contractor to meet the delivery schedule. Any assistance rendered to the contractor on this contract or acceptance by the government of delinquent goods or services hereunder will be solely for the purpose of mitigating damages and is not to be construed as an intention on the part of the government to condone any delinquency, or as a waiver of any rights the government may have under subject contract. INTERRUPTION OF SERVICE The contractor recognizes that the services under this contract are critical to the government and must continue without interruption. Contractor also recognizes that when the contract expires, a successor, either the government or another contractor, may continue the services. The contractor agrees to furnish phase-in-training, apply its best efforts and cooperation to carry out an orderly and efficient transition to a successor. DISSEMINATION OF INFORMATION There shall be no dissemination or publication, except within and between the contractor and any subcontractors, of information developed under this contract or contained in the reports to be furnished pursuant to this contract without prior written approval from the contracting officer.

RELEASE OF REPORTS The contractor is prohibited from releasing to any source, other than the sponsoring activity, any interim, draft and final reports or information pertaining to services performed under this contract until report approval or official review has been obtained. Furthermore, the contractor shall insure that the cover of all interim, draft and final reports contain the following statement: "The view, opinions, and/or findings contained in this report are those of the author(s) and should not be construed as an official government position, policy or decision, unless so designated by other documentation."

SOFTWARE RIGHTS a. All software to provide under this contract shall be delivered with unlimited rights in accordance with the provisions of FAR 52.227-14. b. If at any time during the term of the contract, the contractor determines that it is more advantageous to the government to incorporate a package, subroutine or module that cannot be provided to the government with unlimited rights into the system, the contractor shall notify the contracting officer in writing. Such notification shall include as a minimum, the name of the item to be furnished with restricted rights and cost saving or other benefits accruing to the government. c. If the contractor and the government mutually agree to incorporate such software package, subroutine or module into the system, the government requires that it be given as a minimum the following rights: (1) Use computer software with the computer for which or with which it was acquired, including use at any government installation to which the computer may be transferred by the government; (2) Use computer software with a backup computer if the computer for which or with which it was acquired is inoperative; (3) Copy computer programs for safekeeping (archives) or backup purposes; (4) Modify computer software, or combine it with other software, subject to the provisions that those portions of the derivative software incorporating restricted rights software are subject to the same restricted rights. The contract shall be modified to set forth the software restrictions and rights of the government. The contractor shall not incorporate such software without a written modification to the contract. d. If the contractor includes any software packages, routines or modules developed at the contractor's expense in the system without identifying it to the contracting officer, all such software shall be considered delivered with "unlimited rights". If the program maintenance of the system is dependent on the source code of any such software, the contractor shall provide the source code and rights to the source code for the life of the system at the time the software and documentation is delivered to the government. TYPE OF SERVICE a. The government and the contractor understand and agree that the services delivered by the contractor to the government are non-personal services. The parties also recognize and agree that no employer-employee or masterservant relationship exists or will exist between the government and the contractor. The contractor and the contractor's employees are not employees of the Federal Government and are not eligible for entitlement and benefits given federal employees. b. Contractor personnel under this contract shall not:

PROCUREMENT SENSITIVE ­ SEE FAR 3.104 Page 16

(1) Be placed in a position where there is an appearance that they are employed by a Federal Officer, or are under the supervision, direction, or evaluation of a Federal Officer. (2) Be placed in a position of command, supervision, administration or control over personnel or personnel of other government contractors, or become a part of the government organization. (3) Be used in administration or supervision of procurement activities. GOVERNMENT FURNISHED PROPERTY AND SERVICES a. The government may furnish the contractor property, service, or information when so doing would be in the Best Interest of the government. Government furnished property and/or services will be specified in the SOW and Section J; Attachment III. b. The property is to be furnished in an "as-is" condition and the government recommends you inspect the property. c. All GFE will be provided to the contractor by the end of the transition period.

ALL ITEMS TO BECOME PROPERTY OF THE GOVERNMENT Title to all sources data and materials furnished by the government, together with all plans, system analysis and design specifications and drawings, completed programs except priority programs and documentation thereof, reports and listings, and all other items pertaining to the work and services to be performed under orders pursuant to this contract, including any copyright shall become and remain with the government upon completion. The government shall have the full right to use each of these for its purposes without compensation or approval on the part of the contractor. The government shall have access to and the right to make copies of the above mentioned items. All proprietary programs shall be indicated as such in individual proposals.
